Article 6, Zhang

Current Affairs Commentary

Freedom of the Seas and American Neutrality by Yan

The high seas are not subject to the jurisdiction of any nation. This is a fundamental principle of international law. Therefore, a country's ships on the high seas in peacetime can be considered its own active territory and should not be interfered with by others. However, in times of international war, the right of belligerent navies to search neutral ships is still generally recognized by all countries. If contraband destined for the enemy country is discovered as a result of the search, it can naturally be confiscated. Whether enemy goods not of a contraband nature can be treated in the same way is a major question. According to the 1856 Declaration of Paris, all belligerent goods transported by neutral ships and all neutral goods transported by belligerent ships, except for contraband, are not subject to confiscation by the enemy. The provisions are very clear. Unfortunately, during the European War, first the German submarine policy, followed by the retaliatory actions of Britain and France, deprived neutral countries of their freedom of navigation. The spirit of the Declaration of Paris was completely lost. Whether the principles in the Declaration of Paris will be respected by belligerents in future wars is difficult to predict. Moreover, there is no legal standard for the nature of so-called contraband. Since the viewpoints of belligerent and neutral countries differ, disputes are inevitable.

The United States has always upheld the principle of freedom of the seas, believing that belligerents should give the greatest respect to the freedom of navigation and commerce of neutral countries. President Wilson made a "Fourteen Points" declaration in January 1918, which stated that there should be absolute freedom of navigation on the seas... except when the seas are blockaded in whole or in part by international action for the enforcement of international covenants. Wilson, recognizing that the United States' participation in the previous war stemmed from the need to uphold the principle of freedom of the seas, wanted to respect this principle through international cooperation to avoid repeating the same mistakes in the future.

However, given the intensity of modern warfare and the magnitude of its sacrifices, any country, once drawn into the vortex, is only concerned with defeating the enemy and does not care about international faith. Even if there are agreements to respect freedom of the seas in peacetime, it is not impossible for them to break their promises in wartime to implement their operational objectives. If a neutral country only argues verbally, it will not help in the slightest. It must either willingly concede or use force to defend its neutral rights. Willing concessions are one thing; however, using force as a tool to defend neutrality inevitably leads to abandoning the status of neutrality and entering the war. During the last European War, the United States almost broke with Britain before declaring war on Germany, precisely because the British undermined its freedom of the seas and neutral status in every way. The reason it later joined forces with the British to fight against Germany was that the British damaged American property, while the Germans damaged American lives. When weighing property against life, life is of course more important. From this perspective, since the Americans cannot be sure that future belligerents will respect their freedom of the seas and do not want to maintain their neutral status by force, there is no other way but to revise their traditional policies.

In recent days, talk of the United States revising its neutrality principles has been rife. Upon observing the inside story, we know that this is no accident. The significance of this matter is that, first, it indicates that the brewing of a second world war is becoming increasingly mature. The United States is making this gesture to make clear its desire not to be drawn into the war. Second, it is a message to Japan that, in future international wars, the United States, while unwilling to engage in military conflict with Japan lightly, will also not allow its policy of maintaining freedom of the seas to restrict the actions of those fighting against Japan. Third, it is to foster goodwill with the British, so they will know that, in any future situation, conflict between Britain and the United States is unlikely. Since British territories are spread all over the world, once it enters the war, it will inevitably affect the entire globe. If the British refuse to abandon their right to search neutral ships and blockade enemy ports, and the Americans insist on their policy of freedom of the seas, conflict between the two countries will be difficult to avoid. Conversely, if the Americans are willing to automatically concede, it will greatly facilitate British operations. Since Britain and the United States have this tacit understanding, even the strong Japanese will not dare to act rashly.

Britain, America, and Japan Wasted Words

Naval Negotiations Adjourned

Three Countries Issue Joint Declaration

Reconvening in the Near Future Uncertain

Britain and Japan Continue Technical Consultations

(London) The preliminary naval conference of the three countries, which began here at the end of June, was officially announced to be adjourned this afternoon. Delegations from the UK, US and Japan held a plenary session in the House of Commons. British Prime Minister MacDonald chaired the meeting and stated that the UK would take appropriate measures to reconvene naval talks when the time was ripe. The American representative Davis and Japanese representative Matsudaira then delivered replies. (19th Reuters)

Issuing a Communiqué

(London) All representatives of the British, American, and Japanese delegations participating in the preliminary London naval talks gathered at the office of Prime Minister MacDonald in the House of Commons this afternoon for the final plenary session. It was announced that the preliminary naval talks would be postponed indefinitely. After the meeting, the following communiqué regarding the postponement of the naval talks was issued to the press:

"This afternoon, the British, American, and Japanese delegations discussed various matters related to the postponement of the preliminary naval talks in the House of Commons. The meeting was chaired by British Prime Minister MacDonald. Attendees included, from the American side, Chief Delegate Davis, Chief of Naval Operations Stanley, Counselor of the Embassy in the UK Atherton, Naval Expert Captain Dumann Schumann, Major Duncan, Field, and Lieber, among others; from the Japanese side, Chief Delegate Ambassador to the UK Matsudaira, Chief Expert Major General Yamamoto, and Experts Kato, Iwashita, Mizota, among others; and from the British side, Prime Minister MacDonald, Foreign Secretary Simon, First Lord of the Admiralty Monsell, Admiral Sir Chatfield, and Vice Admiral Liddell-Crichton, among others. As a result of the discussions, it was unanimously agreed that these talks, which began in June of this year and have continued to this day, October 23, were beneficial. These talks were originally intended to prepare for the future naval conference stipulated by the 1930 London Naval Treaty. After various suggestions were made, the scope of the talks expanded, and candid and friendly discussions were held on all aspects of naval issues. The purpose of the preliminary talks was not to reach an urgent conclusion, but only to prepare for the future naval conference to establish an agreement. France and Italy are also signatories to the current naval treaty, so they participated in the discussions when the preliminary talks were held in the summer of this year. The progress of the talks has been continuously notified to those two countries. Although the three governments attending these talks support continued limitation of naval armaments and reduction of naval forces to the extent agreed upon by all relevant countries, the principles and methods required to achieve this goal remain to be determined. The current talks have reached a considerable stage. The representatives of the three countries believe that it is appropriate to announce a postponement at this time so that the representatives of each country can take the opportunity to consult with their respective governments in person and make a more thorough analysis and consideration of the situation created by the results of the talks. Therefore, the representatives of the three countries unanimously agreed that the naval talks should be postponed for the time being. At the same time, the governments of the countries related to the London talks should maintain close contact with each other and, even more so, with the other contracting parties to the London and Washington treaties. The postponement of the talks will also provide the British government with an opportunity to consult with the governments of the British dominions. Furthermore, in terms of the preparatory work completed by past talks, it is hoped that the situation will develop in such a way that the next round of talks can be held quickly when the appropriate time is reached. As the initiator of this preliminary round of talks, Britain should take appropriate steps for the next round of talks." (19th Havas)

Simon's Broadcast Address

Japan is Free to Abolish the Naval Treaty

Believes a New Naval Agreement is Not Hopeless

Maintaining Security is Especially Important for Britain

(London) Foreign Secretary Simon gave a radio broadcast speech this evening, commenting on the manner in which the naval negotiations were postponed. He declared that the naval negotiations may be reopened in two or three months. In his speech, Simon said, "Japan will, no later than this month, namely December, notify the abrogation of the Washington Naval Treaty. Regarding this matter, the Japanese government no longer attempts to conceal it. This is indeed something we deeply regret. However, it must be understood that Japan has the complete freedom to notify the abrogation of the treaty, and no one has the right to oppose it. Furthermore, it is inappropriate to be overly pessimistic about this action by Japan. It should be known that after the Washington Naval Treaty is notified for abrogation, it still has a valid period of two years. (Note: The Washington Naval Treaty is scheduled to expire at the end of 1936.) During this period, various countries can establish a new naval agreement. If this does not happen, if countries fail to conclude a treaty in the future to limit the total tonnage of naval forces and the maximum tonnage of warships of each class, the whole world will encounter a terrible disaster. The efforts of the past regarding disarmament have been remarkably effective, like the Washington and London naval treaties. These two naval treaties have saved the countries involved hundreds of millions of dollars, provided each country with a sense of security, and fostered mutual cooperation to safeguard peace. We are determined to do everything possible to preserve this system in the future, precisely for this reason. The British Empire has responsibilities to its vast dominions and colonies that it cannot abandon. Therefore, we will not compromise on anything necessary for our country's security. At the same time, we must also put ourselves in the position of other countries, give consideration to them, and cooperate with them in an effort to establish a plan that is agreed upon by all countries. This plan must ensure that all countries receive fair treatment and must include the principles I put forward in the House of Commons the other day. What were these principles? That 'equality of security is the right of all nations.' "Simon continued, stating that Japan had put forward several proposals, the gist of which was to establish a new basic system to replace the current naval treaty. This basic system would allow countries to build warships to achieve what is called "the common maximum limit." Therefore, we believe that Japan's implementation of naval construction to reach the common maximum limit is the inevitable result of this proposal by Japan. Japan originally wanted to take this step and considered it timely, so it demanded the right to determine the naval forces that reach the common maximum limit. However, in our view, there are other ways to achieve equality of security. We believe that since the territory of our United Kingdom spans Asia and Europe, and the British territories spread all over the world are not included in this calculation, it is essential for Britain to have a larger navy in order to maintain equality of security. To illustrate, other countries' navies may be able to concentrate in the Pacific, but the British navy is not allowed to concentrate entirely in the Pacific. As for establishing a new agreement base, although the period is still far away and requires a long period of effort, I can tell you that, while I do not ask any country to abandon the principles they deem most important, we are already bound to find a way to establish a basis that is acceptable to all parties, so that the world does not encounter the scourge of unlimited arms competition after the current treaty expires. The British government was the initiator of this preliminary naval talks. When the time is right, the UK should take appropriate steps. In short, without these preliminary talks, and the rationality we have shown in the preliminary talks, the future formal naval conference may not be successful." (19th Havas)

Japanese Representatives Remain in London

Continuing Technical Discussions

US Representatives Scheduled to Return Home at the End of the Month

(London) Reuters has learned from the US delegation that the US representatives believe that today's communiqué explains the current situation in great detail, summarizes the internal situation accurately, and is able to comprehensively cover the position of the US. The fact that the communiqué does not mention a date for the resumption of talks is particularly comforting to the US. It is reported that from today until the end of the year, British and Japanese representatives will hold talks on technical matters, while the US representatives will leave the UK at the end of the month. British representatives said that this adjournment is a true adjournment. The future goal is to prepare through normal and diplomatic channels for the reopening of discussions before the 1935 General Assembly, so that the General Assembly can be successful. It is expected that the start of diplomatic contact will be after Japan abrogates the Washington Naval Treaty. At that time, what will be discussed will be the British plan based on the exchange of shipbuilding programs. If the opinions of the three countries are close, they will try to resume talks. It is heard that the UK's view on Japan's cancellation of the Washington Naval Treaty is considered extremely serious, but it feels that the declaration of abrogation of the treaty has not diminished the hope of a compromise in the future. The UK has not seen any signs that Japan wants to abolish the Nine-Power Treaty and the Four-Power Treaty on the Pacific; it only feels that Japan wants to negotiate a new naval treaty. (19th Reuters)

Clever British Tactics

UK and US Differ on View of Abolition

(London) The preliminary naval talks have come to an end with the joint declaration, but since before and after the talks, the most skillful diplomatic tactics have undoubtedly been those of the British government. It has maintained contact with the Japanese delegation with its compromise trial, and has maintained its close relationship with the US delegation with its neither close nor distant relationship.

As for the views of the UK and US on Japan's abrogation of the Washington Naval Treaty, they are completely different. The US delegation believes that abrogation is an act of destroying the collective peace mechanism, while the British government authorities believe that abrogation should be viewed as insignificant as much as possible. The abrogation of a treaty is like terminating a lease agreement and has no other meaning. It is now like staying in the rented house and signing a new lease in order to ensure its favorable conditions. This observation is quite intriguing. (20th Japanese Allied News)

After Japan Abrogates Treaty

US Response Steps

Navy Constantly Ready to Take Necessary Actions

Naval Base Seeks to Restore Defensive Works

| Swanson's Statement |

(Washington) Today, members of the press visited Secretary of the Navy Swanson and asked how the US shipbuilding program would proceed after Japan abrogated the Washington Naval Convention. Swanson replied, "Our Navy is always at sea." Swanson also said that according to the terms of the treaty, it will remain in effect for two years after abrogation. We should take the necessary and proper steps to protect the United States and its industries. Swanson also answered another question, stating that the decision to complete the naval base defense program, which was suspended after the signing of the Washington Naval Convention, is now being retained. (19th Reuters)

French Foreign Minister Receives Japanese Ambassador

Discusses Naval Issues

Explains Reasons for Not Being Able to Jointly Abrogate Treaty

(Paris) French Foreign Minister Laval held a lengthy talk with the Japanese Ambassador to France to discuss the adjournment of the naval talks and the Japanese cabinet's decision to announce the abrogation of the naval treaty. Mr. Laval reiterated that France, due to diplomatic and strategic considerations, could not take joint action to abrogate the Washington Naval Treaty. (20th National News)

A Glimpse of British and American Public Opinion

Japan Threatens World Peace

Adjournment is a Sign of Failure

(Washington) Republican Senator Borah believes that Japan's announcement of the abrogation of the Washington Naval Treaty is regrettable, but the United States cannot infer from this that Japan is adopting a challenging attitude towards the United States. Senator Steiwer of Oregon said that Japan's attitude is a threat to peace, but his tone is still moderate. As for the New York Post, it said that Japan is defying all countries in the world. The World Telegram said that the world is about to engage in an arms race, and the initiator is Japan. The State Department made no comment on the decision of the Japanese Privy Council. (Note: The Japanese Privy Council held a meeting in the Imperial Presence today and unanimously endorsed the Japanese government's decision to abrogate the Washington Naval Treaty.) It is generally believed that the naval powers will reopen the conference in 1936, and Soviet Russia may also participate. We should wait quietly for this period to come. Before 1936, the naval arms race will not begin, because until 1936, the principles set by the Washington Naval Treaty will still be observed by other signatories and Washington. (Note: The Washington Naval Treaty must be announced for abrogation two years before the expiration date, but it will continue to be valid for two years after the announcement of abrogation.) (19th Havas)

(London) Most newspapers here have commented on the announcement of the adjournment of the naval talks this morning. The Labour Party's organ, the Daily Herald, and the Liberal news organ, The News Chronicle, both believe that the adjournment is a sign of failure. (20th Havas)

(London) Those criticizing the adjournment of the naval talks today all lament that there were no more obvious results, but they acknowledge that these talks have laid the foundation for future negotiations. They believe that since the Washington Naval Treaty still has two years of validity, there is ample time to find a way to replace the arms race. The Times of London said that the diplomacy of the British representatives was indeed proper. Their role as mediators has earned them considerable trust from both the US and Japan, and the falsity and harmfulness of the British-Japanese secret agreement is self-evident. The Washington Treaty has given the signatories many benefits. Now that Tokyo has abolished it, it bears a heavy responsibility. However, since Tokyo has said that the abrogation of the treaty is only a means of concluding a new treaty, it can be seen that the three countries have one purpose, namely to establish a new treaty as good as the old one. The Daily Telegraph mentioned the issue of face, saying that trying to satisfy the feelings of the Japanese, who are ashamed and angry, will make the hope of resolving major issues in the Far East turn into a mirage. The current stalemate, which is not yet dangerous, may easily become dangerous. If the solution remains unresolved, then Britain and its autonomous territories must jointly deliberate on the most difficult British Empire policy problem rarely encountered by British politicians. (20th Reuters)

US Builds New Type of Aircraft Carrier

Oil Tank Retrofitting Postpones Launch

(Washington) Secretary of the Navy Swanson stated today that the launch of the US's newest aircraft carrier, the USS Ranger, has been postponed for several months. Secretary Swanson stated that the steel used to build the ship's fuel tanks is susceptible to corrosion from gasoline, so it must all be replaced. Navy officials hope that the USS Ranger can participate in naval exercises to be held in the North Pacific next May. (19th National Press)

Defense of Panama Canal is of Utmost Importance

Twenty Suicide Squads Can Destroy it in Half a Day

Japanese Fishermen Using Weighted Lines to Measure Depth

American Magazine Publishes Article Urging People to Wake Up

(New York) The owner of the Panama American Magazine, published in Panama City, Panama, Lance Vaneval, stated here today that a suicide squad of twenty people could destroy the Panama Canal into powder within twelve hours. This action is easy to accomplish, but the result could make the canal unusable for commercial shipping for a long time. Although repairs can be carried out immediately, it cannot be opened soon, because there are still some important locations in the canal that are completely undefended. The Panama American Magazine has repeatedly published articles urging people to wake up. Although the army authorities have now increased the defense forces, the most important locations still have no defenses. Mr. Lance went on to say that 75 percent of the Japanese living in the Canal Zone have no fixed income. Barbershops do not cut a single hair all day, shirt factories do not sell a single shirt all day, and restaurants do not cook a single dish all day. The fishing rods used by fishermen are made of steel wire and lead bait, with no hooks at the end, so their work is clearly measuring the depth of the canal. The army chief is unwilling to inform civilians of more appropriate ways to protect the canal, so he is indifferent to his articles. The defense of the Panama Canal is almost entirely the responsibility of the US Army in peacetime. Although the Navy has some affiliated warships patrolling various parts of Central America, they are in no way related to the defense of the Panama Canal. (19th National News)

Roosevelt Has No Intention of Opening a New Canal

Answering Questions with Humorous Tone

(Washington) When a guest asked President Roosevelt for his candid opinion on the excavation of the Nicaragua Canal, Mr. Roosevelt replied in a humorous tone, saying that the old Nicaragua Canal Company stocks in his house were so many that they were enough to wallpaper a large room. Mr. Roosevelt's words referred to the previous plans to excavate the canal. The right of the United States to excavate the Nicaragua Canal was obtained in 1916 by signing a treaty with Nicaragua for US$3 million, the use of which must be supervised by the United States. There was a Pacific Railroad along the canal route owned by Nicaragua, but its shares were 51% owned by New York bankers, who then resold them to the American public. When the canal plan failed, these stocks became worthless. President Roosevelt's statement today shows that the government has no intention of opening this canal at this time. (19th National Telegram)

British Prime Minister Writes on the Crisis of War

Arms Race Cannot Be Prevented

Unilateral Disarmament Does Not Help Peace

(London) Prime Minister MacDonald warned today that if Britain replenishes its national defense but cannot avoid the European arms race, then a second European war is unavoidable. The Prime Minister sent this idea in an article to be published in the December issue of the National Labour Party magazine, which was published today. Although the Prime Minister insisted on avoiding the arms race, he also did not agree with setting an example of disarmament, saying that setting an example of disarmament in the eyes of the international community does not help peace. Although Britain has worked hard on disarmament as an advocate for the world, peace is still far away when Britain destroys its last battleship and bomber, and Britain's peace efforts at this time will be in vain. (19th National Telegram)

Ambassador Guo Hosts Reception to Showcase Modern Chinese Paintings

(London) Guo Taiqi, the Chinese Ambassador to the UK, and his wife held a reception at the embassy today to show guests the best of the modern Chinese paintings to be exhibited in London in February next year. Several well-known critics, such as Mr. Pingrong, were present and praised the paintings, saying that they were able to maintain their ancient style and also incorporate world trends to enhance them. The guests all said that Chinese artists' paintings of flowers and birds are still unparalleled. (19th Reuters Telegram)

Franco-Russian Agreement Announced

Political and Commercial Protocols

(Moscow) The protocols signed by Laval and Litvinov in Geneva on December 5 have been announced here as follows:

After exchanging views on the negotiation of the Eastern European Pact, Laval and Litvinov stated that both governments have decided to work towards the conclusion of this pact. At the same time, during the negotiations, both countries are willing to abide by the following principles:

(1) Both governments shall not agree to negotiations with governments invited to join the pact, especially those who have not yet expressed their agreement in principle, for the conclusion of agreements that may hinder the Eastern Regional Pact or are related to it. At the same time, they shall not agree to the conclusion of agreements that are contrary to the spirit held by both governments.

(2) Therefore, both governments shall notify each other of any suggestions made by the government in question to any country that contains such meaning, regardless of the manner in which the suggestion is made.

The protocol stipulates that the same principles and the same objectives shall be observed during and after the negotiation of the aforementioned pact. The above obligations shall be valid in other events that can replace the current activities. Both governments shall not abandon this activity unless they unanimously agree that it is no longer necessary to continue. If both parties believe that this measure is indeed no longer necessary to continue, they shall consult on new guarantees suitable for both parties in the same spirit and purpose.

Both governments firmly believe that the continued and effective guarantee of this Franco-Soviet diplomatic cooperation will be beneficial to the success of the current international negotiations and will strengthen the spirit of mutual trust between the two governments and the two countries. (19th TASS Telegram)

(Moscow) After negotiations on commercial issues between Rosenholz, the Soviet Commissioner of Foreign Trade, and Marchandeau, the French Minister of Commerce and Industry, the Franco-Soviet Commercial Protocol was signed in Moscow on December 9 and came into effect on the 9th. The full text has been announced here. The protocol stipulates that both parties shall begin negotiations as soon as possible to conclude a treaty of commerce and navigation and shall immediately seek to replace the temporary commercial agreement concluded on January 11, 1934, with an agreement of the same nature. For the purpose of concluding this agreement, the following recommendations shall be considered. These recommendations may be regarded as the basis for a new agreement, namely, that the Soviet Union should be allowed to borrow loans on the French market, and the amount, conditions, period and interest rate, etc., must be stipulated later. The loan period must be sufficient, and the interest rate must be normal. Its use is to order goods from French factories, which must be paid within one year. The issue of loan guarantees for French exporters has also been discussed. If this new commercial treaty is not signed before January 1, 1935, the original temporary commercial agreement will continue next year until the new treaty is signed as soon as possible. (19th TASS Telegram)

Agenda of the Eighty-Fourth Session of the League of Nations Council

To Be Convened in Mid-January Next Year

(Geneva) The Executive Council of the League of Nations has decided to hold the 84th regular session on January 11, 1925. The agenda has recently been announced: (1) The issue of the protection of minorities in Albania (The Albanian government recently ordered the abolition of all private schools in the country and replaced them with national schools, which aroused opposition from most of the minorities in the country. At the end of last month, representatives from Peru, Mexico, and the United Kingdom requested the League of Nations to include this matter on the agenda.) (2) The issue of the German minority in the Upper Silesia Province of Poland (Upper Silesia was originally part of Germany, and part of it was assigned to Poland after the war.) (3) The issue of the resettlement of the Assyrian minority in Iraq. (4) The most important issue of the Saar plebiscite. This vote is scheduled to be held on January 13, and the results can be revealed in Geneva on the evening of that day. As for the application submitted by Yugoslavia due to the Marseilles assassination, although it is not included in the agenda of the Executive Council, the British Lord Privy Seal, Eden (i.e., the rapporteur), will report on the implementation of the resolution passed by the Executive Council at its last meeting to resolve the dispute between the two countries of South and Hungary by the Hungarian government. (20th Havas Telegram)

Former Yugoslav Foreign Minister

Ordered to Form a New Cabinet

Belgrade Prince Paul, the Regent of Yugoslavia, has now formally commissioned former Foreign Minister Yevtich to rise up and form a new cabinet. Yevtich entered the palace at noon today to see the Regent. After leaving the palace, he began to contact all parties. Former leaders of the Slovenian Party, Koroshets, and former cabinet members of the extremist faction, Milotic, are all being contacted. This proves that the previous legend that the Regent has instructed Yevtich to form a cabinet can be freely disposed of is reliable. It is said that the purpose of Yevtich's formation of a new cabinet is to create a concentrated cabinet of all factions, which will not only include the opposition faction in the parliament, but also recruit people from the previously disbanded political parties. Furthermore, Yevtich is neither a member of the Senate nor a member of the House of Representatives, and he was also a confidential advisor to the former King Alexander. After Alexander's death, this position was retained in the regency, so Yevtich's position is extremely high, and the convenience of his work is even more obvious. Furthermore, the success of Yevtich's formation of a cabinet is even more predictable because Yevtich has a close relationship with General Zhivkovich, the Chief of the Army, and the general's power is also extremely certain in the Yugoslav political arena. On the Issue of the Eastern European Pact

Germany Expresses Its Attitude

Rome German Foreign Minister Neurath made a statement to the Italian "Messenger Report" reporter in Saar, generally saying that he believes that France has sincerity and goodwill regarding the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact. Neurath believes that if a conflict occurs between the signatory countries, and Germany must send troops to intervene to ensure the permanent invariance of Eastern European territory and politics, then Germany will never agree. When the reporter asked how the Four-Power Pact of England, France, Italy and Germany in 1933 (signed in Rome on July 15) would be joined by other countries such as the Little Entente countries, Neurath politely declined, saying that he hoped not to ask any further questions on this point. British Newspaper Discusses the Silver Issue

(London) The Financial Times published an editorial today stating that since President Roosevelt's silver purchase plan was announced, the silver market has become a largely "paper" market. The amount of silver purchased by the United States is not as much as speculators expected for its price to rise, and coupled with unstable news from China, buyers have become helpless. All of these factors seem to prove that the price of silver will not last long. The newspaper also said that if Sir Sassoon of Shanghai's opinion can be implemented, it can not only alleviate China's difficulties, but also not hinder the United States from proceeding with its silver program. London has no certainty that this opinion will be adopted by President Roosevelt. (20th Reuters Telegram)

Japan Discovers a Gold Bar Smuggling Ring

Two Chinese Arrested

Osaka It has recently been discovered that overseas Chinese in Japan have organized a smuggling ring to smuggle gold bars worth one million yuan. When the Japanese mail ship Shanghai liner Ikoma Maru was docked at the Osaka Port on the afternoon of the 17th, a Chinese man carried a cloth bag onto the ship and put it in the coal bunker and left. The crew suspected his actions and checked his bag, and found 52 gold bars, each six inches long and one inch wide, worth 160,000 yuan at the current price. Therefore, they reported to the police and arrested two Chinese men. As a result of the interrogation, it was provided that the leader of the smuggling ring was Shen Xieji, the owner of Wan Yi Hao, a food and trade merchant in Sakae-cho, Kobe. The authorities immediately sent personnel to search his residence and confiscated 40,000 yuan worth of gold bars and other evidence. However, Shen Yeyu took the Shanghai Maru from Kobe to Shanghai on the 17th, and the authorities relied on wireless

electricity to rely on the captain to arrest the criminal. It is said that Shen is in contact with the headquarters of the smuggling ring in the French Concession of Shanghai, and has so far transported more than one million yuan in gold bars. (20th Japanese Allied Telegram)

(London) The Chinese government's Purchasing Materials Committee today ordered sixteen third-class steel sleeping cars from the Birmingham Railway Vehicle Company in the UK for the southern section of the Yuehan Railway, at a cost of £60,000. Former Japanese Ambassador to the United States

Haniwara Masanao Passes Away

(Tokyo) Haniwara Masanao, the former ambassador to the United States and plenipotentiary to the Washington Conference, passed away at 8:00 a.m. today due to cerebral congestion while recuperating, at the age of 59. His brief resume is as follows: After graduating from the English and Political Science Department of Tokyo Senmon Gakko in the 30th year of the Meiji era, he passed the diplomatic and consular official examination, and was then appointed as a diplomatic official to Xiamen. After that, he served in the United States and Korea, and successively served as embassy secretary, consul general, director of the Commercial Bureau, director of the Political Affairs Bureau, and vice minister of foreign affairs. In the 11th year of the Taisho era, he was appointed as a special envoy and plenipotentiary ambassador to the United States. Later, he returned to his country and waited for orders. In the 10th year of the Taisho era, he also served as a plenipotentiary commissioner to participate in the Washington Conference. (20th Electric News)

Roosevelt Gained Weight

(Washington) The US government believes that the presidential office of the President of the United States is unparalleled in its burden. Some former presidents have fallen ill in office, and some have died in office. President Roosevelt has shouldered the heavy responsibility of revitalization and has worked hard for the country. However, he can handle it competently and happily. President Roosevelt has a physical examination once a year. The doctor finished the examination today and said that his health is even better than when he took office. His weight is 170

Seventy-two pounds can also be said to be a good omen. The president is overworked, and the physical examination has been delayed for two weeks, and it has only been held today. The president declared today that the Congress is about to open, and the government affairs are complicated. He will not have time to do "fireside chats" on the radio before the Congress opens. He Chengjun Arrives in Hankou Yesterday

Liu Xiang presented his plan for governing Sichuan and suppressing bandits in detail, which was highly appreciated by the central government. After careful planning, the central government decided to suppress the bandits again to try to gather the bandits. Liu Duban believed that the results of this trip were satisfactory, so he returned to Sichuan first to deploy everything. The central government also promised to subsidize the Sichuan army with temporary expenses on a monthly basis during the bandit suppression period. As for the bandits who fled from western Jiangxi, after being severely attacked by the Xiang and Gui troops and the chasing troops several times, they have no combat capability. They have recently fled to the border of Guizhou. There are only sporadic small bandits in Xiang territory, but because their main forces have lost contact, they are not enough to be a threat. As for drug prohibition, it is more urgent in Hubei than in other provinces. I hope that the people will work hard and strive to save themselves and the country. In addition, Li Tiancai and others, who were accompanying Zhang Xueliang, also returned to Hankou on the same wheel. (20th Central News Agency Telegram)

There are scattered bandits in southern and western Hubei, which will be wiped out at any time. There are no bandits in central and northern Hubei. The bandits who fled to Xiang and Jiangxi will be suppressed by the Xiang, Qian and Gui troops, which is not a problem. International Commercial Telegrams

丨Special Commercial Telegram from Reuters on December 20th丨

Gold and Silver: English Gold: The London gold price today is 140 shillings, 8.5 pence, down 1 pence.

English Silver: The London silver price rose 1.25, with spot at 24 pence 1875 and futures at 24 pence 3125. Trading was not active, with speculators buying or selling. The market closed steadily.

American Silver: The Mount Lyell silver market, futures rose approximately 10 pounds, with sluggish trading.

Indian Silver: The Bombay silver price showed a strong rise. The spot closing price was 65 rupees 7 annas, 13 annas higher than yesterday's close.

Exchange Rates: English-American: The London foreign exchange market was calm this morning. The opening exchange rate between British and American currencies was $4.943125, lower by 0.0625 than yesterday's American-British close. This price remained unchanged until the time of the telegram. One US dollar equals 4 shillings 0552 pence.

English-French: The opening price remained unchanged at 74 francs 84. Later, it rose 6 pounds, then fell 6 pounds at 2 p.m., returning to 74 francs 84, the same as the opening price.

American-British: In the New York foreign exchange market today, the opening exchange rate between US and British currencies was $4.9425, down 0.125.

Cotton and Wheat: American Cotton: The New York cotton market today showed the sluggish atmosphere of the approaching holiday. Sales were few, and demand was also scarce. The opening price rose slightly, but then a minor rebound occurred due to long position liquidations. The cotton cloth market report indicates brisk business before the holiday. The rumor of goods exchange between the United States and Germany has now been dismissed. Indian Cotton: In the Bombay cotton futures market today, operators purchased, and the sentiment was stable at the close. The price of White Lohi cotton for the April-May period was 229 rupees 125, up 1 rupee 375.

English Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market showed a slightly firmer trend this morning. At 1 p.m., the price for the May period was 6.75, up 2 pounds.

English Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market showed a very slight rebound. At 1 p.m., the price for the May period was 5 shillings 2.25 pence, down half a penny.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market had unsettled sentiment. Opening prices fell slightly due to extremely low demand. Observers say that the wheat market lacks leadership. According to the weather report, the spring wheat region is currently experiencing blizzards, and the weather in the coarse grains region is even colder.

Rubber: London: The London rubber market was stable. At noon, the trading price for the April-June period was 6.5625 pence, the same as yesterday.

New York: The New York rubber market opened more sluggishly than yesterday. There was hardly any change within the first hour after opening.

Securities: New York: Before the opening of the New York securities market, favorable factors included continued positive news about general businesses, while unfavorable factors included the unsettled trend of public utility stocks, increasing uncertainty. However, long position liquidations were less than expected. Today's securities market is expected to be active at the opening, with small and uneven price fluctuations and occasional buyers. However, public utility securities are again under pressure, and confidence has been disturbed, so the continued downward trend of the market is also expected. The prices are as follows:

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Party Department has scheduled a meeting on the 28th, gathering committee members from the Jiangdu and other twelve county party departments involved in the Huai River inland sea project, to discuss strategies for assisting in guiding the Huai River. (20th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Jiangsu Department of Finance Improves Land Tax Collection

(Zhenjiang) In order to improve land tax collection and eliminate the malpractices of treasury clerks, the Jiangsu Department of Finance has specially begun a pilot program in Kunyi, Jiazhen, and other counties where land surveys have been completed. Tax collection offices will be established in local banks to handle the task, in order to prevent clerks from engaging in corruption. (20th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Tianjin Circles Form Comfort Team to Jiangxi

(Tianjin) Tianjin circles are forming a comfort team to Jiangxi to comfort the victorious troops who quelled the Red uprising. Each organization, including the Municipal Party Department, Provincial and Municipal Government, Chamber of Commerce, Educational Association, representatives from secondary schools and above, and press representatives, will send one to three people. The Provincial and Municipal Governments will each contribute $2,000, and the Party Department will contribute $1,000, as comfort expenses. Prizes will also be solicited from various circles. The team is scheduled to depart on the 25th, for a round trip of two weeks. (20th Special Dispatch)

Liu Guitang's Troops Maraud Hebei Territory

(Tianjin) Over 300 of Liu Guitang's bandit troops, having fled from eastern Chahar, have entered Hebei territory. They burned and looted over a hundred households in Wanghuai Town, Fuping County, and kidnapped the township head and deputy. On the 16th, they fled from Fuping to Lingshou County, where they robbed the villagers of Chenzhuang Town, Willow Garden, and other places of all their property. They intend to raid Pingshan County again. Currently, the entire Pingshan County militia has been mobilized and deployed to guard the Hui Kou Village and Guo Su Town, where Lingshou and Pingshan Counties meet. The county magistrate and the militia leader are personally directing the defense. (20th Special Dispatch)
