Northwest Inspection Notes by Our Special Correspondent Geng Ya

Overview of Hami

(I) Historical Background: Hami was the land of Iwoluo during the Han Dynasty, belonging to the Xiongnu. Emperor Ming conquered it, establishing the Yihuo Commandant. During the Three Kingdoms period, it belonged to the Xianbei. Zhang Jun of the Former Liang Dynasty of the Jin Dynasty occupied it. During the Northern Wei Dynasty, it belonged to the Rouran. In the twelfth year of Emperor Wen's Taihe reign, it became affiliated with the city. Later, the Later Wei Dynasty became Shanshan and Turpan. The Western Turks occupied it. In the sixth year of Emperor Yang of the Sui Dynasty, the Yiwu Prefecture was established. After the Sui Dynasty's chaos, it was again occupied by the Western Turks. In the fourth year of Emperor Taizong of the Tang Dynasty, it surrendered and the Xi Yizhou was established. Later, it was renamed Yizhou. In the early years of Tianbao, it became Yiwu Prefecture. In the early years of Qianyuan, it was restored to Yizhou (governing the three counties of Yiwu, Rouyuan, and Nazhi). After Guangde, it was lost to Tubo. The Chen family occupied its land. From the Kaiyuan period of the Tang Dynasty until the early Song Dynasty, it lasted for ten generations. After Yongxi, it belonged to the Asalan Uyghur of Xizhou. During the Yuan Dynasty, it was called Hamil, under the control of the Uyghur of Huozhou. In the Yongle period of the Ming Dynasty, Chief Anke Temuer surrendered and was enfeoffed as the Prince of Zhongshun, establishing the Hami Guard. After Zhengde, it was occupied by Chief Mangsur of Tubo, who closed the Jiayu Pass and abandoned Hami. Later, it re-affiliated with the early Qing Dynasty. The Hami Guard Hui and Er Du surrendered. When it came to Tuluntai as king, he assisted Guo Dong of the Hexi Hui in rebellion and was executed. In the twenty-sixth year of Kangxi, Chief Erbeidula captured and offered Galdan's son, and was granted the Zhasake seal, beginning its internal affiliation. During the Qianlong reign, the Hami Office was established. In the early years of Guangxu, it was changed to a province and promoted to a directly governed office. In the second year of the Republic of China, it was changed to Hami County, with three cities: Hui, Han, and Xin, forming a triangular formation. The Hui and Han cities are very high and solid. The ramparts of the Xin city were mostly destroyed.

(II) Area: It is 1,015 li long from east to west and varies in width from north to south, with some parts as wide as 950 li. The area is at least over 400,000 square li.

(III) Population: The entire county has 3,108 households of Chanshi people, totaling 17,728 people. There are 218 households of Han people, totaling 723 people. There are 340 households of Hui people, totaling 586 people. Statistics show approximately 3,600 households, with over 20,000 people. (Note: There are over 5,000 yurts of Kazakhs within the territory, with each household having between three and five people. Their livelihood is nomadic and unstable, so they are not included in the fixed population count.)

(IV) Mountains, Rivers, and Terrain: There are two rivers flowing in the suburbs of the city area. One is called "Subashi River," originating from Subashi Lake, four li north of the city. The lake is crescent-shaped, with springs gushing year-round without drying up. The area is ten zhang higher than the plain. The spring water flows southwest, encircling the north of the city, dividing into three canals to irrigate the suburbs, vegetable gardens, and melon fields, benefiting the farmers. The other is called "Shenbatu River," originating from the Elm Tree Gully of the East Mountain north of the city, flowing through the villages of Shichengzi, Xiaowan, and Sebashi, irrigating over a thousand mu of land. Initially, it flows southeast, then turns southwest, encircling the south of the city and entering Xiaonan Lake, merging with the Subashi River to the South Lake (70 li south of the city), and then disappearing into the sand. The terrain of Hami is high in the northeast and flat and low in the southwest, shaped like a rolled mat. There are no villages in the southeast, being an endless Gobi Desert. Villages are distributed in the southwest like scattered chess pieces. The northeast and northwest are the continuous areas of the eastern part of the Tianshan Mountains, with towering peaks, known as natural barriers. The Chanshi people use it as a base.

(V) Commerce: Hami's commerce is still in its nascent stage. Its social organization and commercial elements account for only about 2% of the population. Apart from the local Chanshi and Hui people, there are only a dozen or so merchants from Pingjin, Jin, and Sui. The goods they trade in are nothing more than brick tea, cigarettes, and cloth. Furthermore, due to the impact of finance, they cannot engage in fixed trade. The market lacks cash, and the value of provincial notes fluctuates unpredictably, thus promoting a state of exchange between goods and raw materials. For example, merchants from Pingjin, Jin, and Sui exchange tea bricks, cigarettes, silk, and other goods for the sheepskin, wool, camel hair, dried melon, and raisins of the Chanshi people. Since the center of commerce is biased towards mutual exchange of goods, cash transactions gradually become sluggish and quiet. At the same time, the market price of goods entering and leaving also increases daily. The market prices of major imports and exports for September of this year are listed as follows (in yuan):

Exports: Camel Hair 20.00 (per 100 catties)

Wool 1.40 (per 100 catties)

Lambskin 0.30 (per piece)

Cotton 16.00 (per 100 catties)

Raisins 20.00 (per 100 catties)

Fox Fur 4.00 (per piece)

Imports: Brick Tea 2.20 (per brick)

Secondary Tea 2.50 (per brick)

Cigarettes (Hatamen) 3.00 (per pack)

Sugar 0.50 (per catty)

Cloth (Russian goods, such as printed cloth) 0.15 (per dang, approximately 2 chi long)

In recent months, because raw materials are almost exhausted and goods are becoming increasingly difficult to sell, there will be a return to cash transactions. Therefore, although the value of provincial notes was as low as 500 taels (per yuan) in September, it has now returned to 400 taels. At the same time, the prices of the above-listed imported goods are also gradually falling. However, considering the obstructed transportation and the difficulty of sourcing goods, the increase in the price of goods and the decrease in the value of provincial notes will still be a phenomenon that Hami will inevitably see in the future. Fortunately, recently, the new Sui automobiles can now reach Hami, and the province plans to open traffic to Hami to connect with the new Sui route. In the future, Hami's commerce will definitely have considerable development.

There is one thing that urgently needs attention: how to develop commerce in the border areas. Chinese merchants have traditionally lacked organization and have few long-term plans. Their initial motivation for doing business in the border areas is merely to seek double the profit, with the driving force coming from selfishness and self-interest. Therefore, merchants here often say, "Business today is much worse than when we followed Zuo Zongtang's army as merchants (Gan Daying). In the past, there were no taxes, but now there are tax checkpoints everywhere. In the past, profits were ten times higher, but now we worry about losses and even bankruptcy." Listening to their words, it can be seen that the crisis facing Chinese merchants is becoming increasingly acute. Now, the border market is increasingly open, and recently, the Soviet Union, which is close at hand, has reached an agreement to establish an international trading company in Hami. If unorganized and unplanned Chinese merchants compete with foreign merchants who have vast capital and strict organization, their inferior situation and defeat are inevitable.

(VI) Rural Economy: Although Hami has a vast area, arable land accounts for only about 1% of the total area. Currently, there are rural areas and arable land in the northeast district, including Qincheng, Jiji Tai, Tuhulu, Naomao Lake, Huanglu Gang, Yikeshu, Shichengzi, and Yushugou. The southwest district includes the various forts from Tou Er San Si Wu and Da Xiaonan Lake. The northwest includes the various gulleys from Yi Er San Si Wu Liu Qi Ba Jiu and Shazao Yuan. There are approximately 3,000 farming households, with over 90,000 mu of arable land. On average, each household can cultivate 30 mu of land. Each stone of arable land can sow two stones of seeds and harvest twenty stones. Each stone is valued at 7,000 taels of provincial notes (equivalent to 17.5 yuan). After paying a tax of 5% (i.e., eight dou of wheat are collected for each stone of arable land), the annual harvest is valued at over 300 yuan. The living conditions of farmers here are actually better than in other provinces, and the burden is also lighter than elsewhere. Tenant farmers account for approximately 5% of the total number of farmers in the county. Their treatment and wages, such as for annual laborers, were 30 to 40 yuan per person ten years ago, but now, due to the sharp drop in the value of the provincial notes, they are only worth about 10 yuan. However, meals are provided, and sometimes this includes children and wives. Long-term workers receive 1,000 taels of provincial notes per month (equivalent to 2.5 yuan), and short-term workers receive 100 taels per day (equivalent to 0.25 yuan), with meals provided, and some even provide clothing. In addition to a large amount of wheat, rural production also includes animal husbandry. Taking sheep as an example, the annual production is approximately 200,000 heads. On average, each household can raise 70 sheep. Each sheep is valued at 4.5 yuan (the annual wool production is four catties, worth a total of 50 cents, each sheepskin is worth 40 cents, each sheep intestine is worth 10 cents, and 20 catties of mutton are worth 4 yuan).

In total, it is valued at approximately 305 yuan. If scientific methods are used and properly managed, the annual output should be more than this. In addition, the annual production of dried melons and camel hair is also significant. Therefore, the rural society of Hami is still in a feudal and relatively well-off state.

The sources of wealth in Hami's rural economy are: (1) the benefits of irrigation from the snowmelt of the Tianshan Mountains. The eastern part of the Tianshan Mountains spans the county, and snow accumulates year-round. When it melts in spring and summer, the southern flow becomes canal water, and all arable land is irrigated. The northern flow becomes the Caohu Lake, with lush water and grass, suitable for animal husbandry. The recent eastward migration of the Kazakhs is also because the water and grass on the northern slope of the Tianshan Mountains can be used for living. (2) The feudal barriers in the countryside have not yet been broken by capitalist forces, so in a certain sense, they still present a relatively well-off phenomenon. The Chanshi and Hui people of Hami are mostly natives, that is, a type of Oirat people. They are peaceful, hardworking, and both men and women can engage in labor. Moreover, since Abedula ascended the throne, passing through more than ten generations, the people's cultivated land is all received from the Wangfu, and the Wangfu's land is mostly fertile. (3) The population is sparse. Considering the total area of Hami, an average of one person occupies 80 square li. The sparseness of the population can be said to be extreme. As for the wealth of the Chanshi people and the slowness of population reproduction, it is actually inversely proportional.

(VII) Products: Since Hami's social organization is centered on agriculture, its main production is also dominated by agricultural products. The annual production of the county's main agricultural products is estimated to be 180,000 stones of wheat, 230,000 catties of Hami melons, 200,000 sheepskins, 1,000,000 catties of wool, and 150,000 catties of camel hair. In addition, there is also the production of grapes, apples, cabbage, etc., but the quantity is not large. The coal mines in Sandao Ling, 180 li west of the city, originally produced coal, but the mines are low and humid, making mining difficult. The local people dig and extract coal at any time, and the production volume is not accurately统计.

(VIII) The Evolution, Organization, and Current Status of the Hui King: The Zhasake Prince of Hami Hui has two surnames, the ancestor of whom was Ebeidula (first enfeoffed in the 26th year of the Kangxi reign). He was followed by Guobo, then Emin, then Yu'anbu, then Yisake, then Erdesier, then Besier, then Maihamote, then Shmahusote, then Niezi'er, then Besier. The organization consists of two Taiji, who manage military and political affairs; one Kezai, who is in charge of justice; two Mibola, who manage rural water conservancy; 24 Duerga, who manage taxation; 24 Maochi, whose management matters are the same as those of the Duerga, but their powers are smaller and are subject to the command of the Duerga; and 24 Gu Luoman'er, who are assistants to the Maochi. When Shmahusote (that is, the current King Besier's grandfather) was alive, he was able to cooperate well with the province, so his feudal power was also unbreakable. When Jin Shuren governed the new province, he planned to establish Yiwu County in Tuhulu, 300 li north of Hami City, and Yihe County in Sanbao, 180 li west of the city, combining Hami into three counties. He began to measure land, as a preliminary step for establishing governance. The plan was quite complete, but due to repeated irregularities in implementation, conflicts arose with the Hui King's feudal system. Moreover, the fertile land within the territory was owned by the royal family, Taiji, Duerga, etc. As a result, in the 20th year, a peasant revolution-like incident broke out in Hami. On the one hand, it was a head-on conflict between the royal family and officials over land ownership; on the other hand, the royal family and officials fanned the flames and incited competition for national survival, resulting in a complex and chaotic situation that has not yet been fully stabilized.

The current successor to the throne is Besier, the son of Niezi'er. Besier is still young and in poor spirits, and many members of the clan look down on him. His traditional feudalism is now only a remnant of its former self. Moreover, on the other hand, the emerging ruling power of the Chanshi people has turned to other aspects, such as Hojani Yazi, the current deputy chairman of the provincial government, and Yao Leshi, the commander of the Hami garrison. Based on this speculation, the royal autocracy will also "reach its end."

Illegal Parade by Koreans in Beiping

Resentment Against Authorities for Drug Suppression,

Public Demonstration After Assaulting a Tram Conductor

Beiping Dispatch: Since the strict implementation of the drug prohibition policy in the former capital, the authorities have found it particularly difficult to arrest Korean drug dealers. Although the Japanese police ostensibly claim to cooperate with the Chinese authorities in making arrests, in reality, Koreans still receive protection from the Japanese. Recently, cases of Koreans resisting inspections and disobeying arrests by Chinese police have been occurring frequently. Today (18th), another bizarre case of Korean lawlessness occurred. A Korean resident, Kim Dingchen, residing at No. 24 Houcher Hutong, Xizhimen Inner, had a neighbor at No. 23, Duan Jinyu, who was a ticket seller for the tram company. The Korean Kim often engaged in drug dealing, and given the recent arrests of many Korean drug dealers, he felt quite aggrieved. One day, he suddenly saw Duan returning home wearing a blue uniform, and mistakenly identified Duan as a police officer from the Public Security Bureau. Today (18th), he waited in front of his door with a wooden stick. Just as Duan returned from work, Kim suddenly struck Duan on the head from behind with the stick, causing immediate bleeding and a serious injury that knocked Duan to the ground. He was rescued by Inspector Li Songlin of the Fourth District and sent to the Central Hospital for treatment. Kim, seeing the trouble he had caused, not only showed no fear but also gathered more than ten unemployed Koreans and went to the Yichangyong Hotel on Xisi Street to assemble. They then marched in formation and demonstrated on Mashi Street, Yangshi Street, Shuaifu Hutong, and Jinger Hutong, wielding wooden sticks and uttering disrespectful words, as if deliberately provoking trouble. When our police saw this, knowing that reasoning would be futile, they followed secretly, monitoring the situation while providing peaceful protection. This also shows a glimpse of the situation in North China. (18th)

Illegal Organization Discovered in Jixian, War Zone

Actually a So-Called Party of the Poor

Demanding the Abolition of All Taxes

Beiping Dispatch: Recently, a so-called "Party of the Poor," an illegal organization, was suddenly discovered in Jixian. Members of this party, besides local thugs and traitors, also included communist elements. The exact number is not known, but it is estimated to be about four hundred. Their declared aim is "to oppose the payment of any taxes," and they secretly sent party members to Beiping to spread the message. In the past, their activities were secret, so few people knew about them. Recently, the county authorities discovered them. According to a telephone call from Jixian, yesterday (17th) afternoon around 3:00 PM, two people claiming to be "representatives of the Party of the Poor" suddenly went to the county government to petition for a complete exemption from all taxes. County Magistrate Wang Gongbin, because the representatives' origins were unclear, detained them and interrogated them about the "party" organization. Their confessions were roughly as described above. They were placed under guard. In the evening, more than a hundred people claiming to be members of the "Party of the Poor" surrounded the county government, demanding the release of the two representatives, and indicating that if there was no result, they would take certain actions. The county government sent personnel to explain that the matter would be answered after obtaining instructions from higher officials. Until this morning (18th) around 1:00 AM, the county government was still surrounded. After receiving the report, the authorities here were extremely angry. This morning (18th), they instructed the directly governing agency to deal with the matter severely to maintain public order. (18th)

Law on the Implementation of County Autonomy Passed by the Legislative Yuan

The Legislative Yuan convened its 85th meeting on the morning of the 18th of this month and passed (second reading) the Law on the Implementation of County Autonomy. The full text is as follows:

Article 1: Each county government shall, within three months after the promulgation of the County Autonomy Law, divide the townships and districts and organize the neighborhoods in accordance with the provisions of Article 3 of the County Autonomy Law, and report to the provincial government for record.

Article 2: Each township or district shall be named after its original place name or a newly designated place name. The neighborhood names shall be numbered with first, second, etc.

The house numbers for registering the population shall be made of local wood as a principle, and the style shall be determined by the county government.

Article 3: Before the implementation of the County Autonomy Law, all funds and properties managed by the district public offices and all autonomous undertakings shall be taken over by the county government or by the townships independently or jointly.

Article 4: Before the implementation of the County Autonomy Law, anyone who has legally obtained citizenship qualifications shall be a county citizen as defined in Article 6 of the County Autonomy Law.

Article 5: The first township assembly, town assembly, or district assembly after the implementation of the County Autonomy Law shall be convened by the county magistrate.

The first township head, town head, or district head shall be elected by the township assembly, town assembly, or district assembly from three candidates, and the county magistrate shall appoint one of them.

Article 6: If county autonomy has achieved results and is approved by the provincial government, a county council may be established directly in accordance with the provisions of the County Autonomy Law.

In counties where a county council cannot be established, a county council shall be temporarily established, and its organization and election shall be in accordance with the County Council Organization Law and the County Councilors Election Law.

Article 7: Before county magistrates are popularly elected, their appointment shall be in accordance with the County Magistrate Appointment Law.

Article 8: Before county autonomy is completed, the county magistrate may send county government officials to each township to assist the people in carrying out autonomy without additional pay.

Article 9: The "more than 70 percent of the county land tax revenue" mentioned in Article 47, paragraph 1 of the County Autonomy Law shall be more than 60 percent of the total amount of regular and surtaxes on land in the entire county before the implementation of the Land Law.

Article 10: The "30 percent of the county business tax revenue" mentioned in Article 47, paragraph 2 of the County Autonomy Law shall be more than the full amount of the slaughter tax and at least 20 percent of other business taxes before the slaughter tax, tooth tax, and pawn tax are revised in accordance with the Business Tax Law.

Article 11: The township office or town office should be located in a central location in each township.

Article 12: The election and recall of township, town, and district heads, deputy township, town, and district heads, and township, town, and district supervisors in accordance with the County Autonomy Law shall be reported to the county government by the chair of the township assembly, town assembly, or district assembly for record.

After the neighborhood chiefs and lane chiefs are nominated, they shall be reported to the county government by the township office, town office, or district office for record.

Article 13: The general rules for township assemblies, town assemblies, or district assemblies, and the general rules for the operation of township offices, town offices, or district offices shall be determined by the county government, and the detailed rules shall be determined by themselves.

Article 14: The seals of township offices, town offices, or district offices shall be issued by the county government.

Article 15: After a township head, town head, or district head is re-elected, the seal, documents, deeds, funds, and all other items shall be handed over to the new appointee, who shall report to the county government for record after receiving them.

Article 16: The phased progress procedures for national county autonomy shall be determined by the Ministry of Interior.

Article 17: This law shall be implemented from the date of implementation of the County Autonomy Law.

The Law on the Implementation of County Organization, the Law on the Implementation of District Autonomy, and the Law on the Implementation of Township Autonomy shall be repealed from the date of implementation of this law.

Jiangxi Recovered Areas Still Urgently Need Relief

The Provincial Relief Committee Formulates Measures

Appealing to Charitable Organizations to Assist

Nanchang Dispatch: The bandit scourge in Jiangxi lasted for eight years, and after a single suppression, the remaining devastated heavy bandit areas occupy nearly half of the province's area. Each newly recovered area has either been devastated by the Red bandits for a long time, or has been a battlefield for a long time, or has been the rear of the bandits. Houses have been destroyed, stoves have been extinguished, and people have fled. Everywhere is ashes, houses are mounds, and bodies are exposed in the wilderness, gnawed by dogs and wolves, with starving people lying on the road, on the verge of death. There is an urgent need for relief with warm clothing, medicine, and food, with no time to spare. The Provincial Relief Committee specially appeals to charitable organizations from all over to come and provide emergency relief. The measures formulated are roughly as follows:

Burial: The counties of Huichang, Ruijin, Yudu, Ningdu, Guangchang, as well as Hengfeng, Yiyang, Dexing, Leping, Shangrao, Wannian, and Yujiang in eastern Jiangxi, and the counties and towns listed above, are all newly recovered. The fighting has just ended, corpses lie everywhere, and brains and organs are splattered on the ground, a tragic sight. On average, each county and district needs two burial teams, each with five people, with each person receiving two jiao of wages and food per day. For two weeks, this would cost about 8,000 yuan. Medical Care: In the newly recovered areas listed above, as well as refugee centers in Guangchang's Xinan, Toubei Spring, Ningdu's Luokou, Changsheng, etc., temporary clinics have been set up. On average, each needs about 1,000 yuan in medicine expenses.

Emergency Relief: The counties of Ningdu, Shicheng, Ruijin, Yudu, Huichang, Yiyang, Hengfeng, Leping, and Dexing have been severely affected by bandit disasters, and the refugees are the most miserable. On average, each county needs about 3,000 yuan in emergency relief, assuming 2,000 people per county. Also, the counties of Guangchang, Fuliang, Ganxian, Xunwu, Anyuan, Xiushui, Tonggu, Yushan, Guangfeng, Yangxi, Tengtian, Cihua, Wannian, Guixi, Yujiang, Wuyuan, Shangrao, Qianshan, Jiujiang, Ruichang, Suichuan, Wan'an, Ji'an, Taihe, Lianhua, Xiajiang, Xinyu, and Pengze are secondary heavy bandit and drought-stricken areas. On average, each county needs about 2,000 yuan in relief money, assuming 2,000 people per county. As for the method of providing relief, personnel should be sent to conduct on-site assessments and provide relief in exchange for labor, such as repairing embankments and building roads, or lending cattle and seeds for agricultural relief loans. If emergency relief is adopted, it should be done in accordance with the temporary relief distribution methods of this committee.

Shelter: Shelters should be established in suitable locations where refugees from bandit areas can gather widely. In addition to the shelters established by the Provincial Relief Committee in Xingguo, Guangchang, Yudu, Hengfeng, Shangrao, Wannian, Nanfeng, Nancheng, Linchuan, Leping, Dexing, Lianhua, and Ji'an, it is found that there are still several mouths in Ruijin, Huichang, and the Ge Yuan and Fang Dun areas on the border between Hengfeng and Yiyang, where two shelters should be established as necessary. One shelter should be established in Fulin, on the border between the two counties of Wan and Yu, to provide shelter. On average, each shelter can accommodate 3,000 people, which would cost about 12,000 yuan for two months. Warm Clothing: The counties of Ningdu, Ruijin, Shicheng, Huichang, Xingguo, Yudu, and Guangchang have been occupied by bandits for years and have just been recovered. Refugees are returning, and it is the middle of winter. Many are freezing to death because they do not have adequate clothing. In addition to the 10,000 pieces of warm clothing raised by the provincial government from all sectors of society and distributed by the Relief Committee, it is reported that the number of refugees is increasing daily. On average, each county (Ruichang, Huichang, Yudu, Xingguo, Ningdu, and Shicheng) still needs about 2,000 sets of clothing. Furthermore, the newly recovered Fang Dun in Yiyang County, Ge Yuan in Hengfeng County, Lijiatan in Shangrao County, Huanggang in Leping County, Huangpaiwei in Dexing County, Fulin in Wannian County, Daqiao in Yujiang County, and several special districts such as Tengtian, Cihua, and Yangxi are mostly tragic bandit areas. On average, each of the above places also needs 2,000 sets of warm clothing.

Distributing Relief: All of the above-listed areas are the most severely affected and in need of relief. Areas that were previously affected by disasters and have already received relief, and areas that are less severely affected and do not need relief for the time being, have not been included. With the exception of the four counties of Yudu, Huichang, Ningdu, etc., where the highways currently under construction have not yet opened to traffic, new recovered counties and districts such as Guangchang, Hengfeng, Yiyang, Leping, Dexing, Fuliang, Xiushui, Tonggu, Yushan, Qianshan, Wannian, Guixi, Yujiang, Shangrao, Suichuan, Wan'an, Ji'an, Taihe, Ganxian, Lianhua, Xiajiang, Xinyu, Tengtian, Cihua, etc., can be reached directly by car. The counties of Jiujiang, Duchang, and Pengze (drought-stricken) have the convenience of railways and ships. Xunwu is relatively far away, but the counties and districts of Wuyuan and Yangxi can also be reached by car. The journey is peaceful and safe, so you can go to inspect and distribute relief. (December 12-17)

Songjiang

Negotiations Underway Regarding Farmer Injured by Car

On the 16th of this month, there was an incident on the Shanghai-Hangzhou National Highway in the Caoxing section where a farmer was killed by a car. It has been learned that the farmer was from the 12th Tu of Fahua Bridge in Fengxian County. He was walking on the highway and was accidentally hit by car number 6363 from Shanghai, injuring his head. Blood flowed all over the ground, and he fell into a coma. Someone telegraphed the Minhang Station to detain the car. The township police of the Tu are now negotiating with the car owner who caused the accident. The injured farmer has also been sent for medical treatment.

Farmers in Caoxing Robbed and Injured

On the night of the 13th, around 12:00 AM, the home of Lu Qiulin, a farmer from the 7th Tu of Shaxi, Caoxing, was suddenly broken into by seven or eight local-accented bandits, each wielding an iron bar. They forced the victim to hand over his hidden silver. However, Lu did not have any savings, so he was beaten on his limbs. The bandits then robbed him of cloth clothes, money ornaments, and other items, and fled with the stolen goods. The incident was reported to the responsible branch station, which sent police to investigate and confirmed the facts. They issued a loss report and requested the county Public Security Bureau to pursue the robbers.

Suzhou

Two Robbery Cases Solved in One Day

On the 19th, the Criminal Investigation Team of the Public Security Bureau captured six robbers, Zhang Shaoding, Wang Kesheng, Liu Decheng, Zhang Shaohe, Xu Yangmin, and Jiang Juwu, in Lengshuiwan, Fengmen, who were involved in the robbery of Ma Chengji's ointment shop in Bifengfang. They also apprehended Li Yushan (also known as Li Mengbai) and Liu Benfu at Shiqiao Head and recovered a handgun from a manure pit. Zhang Shaoding and others confessed to robbing Ma Chengji's ointment shop and Master Tang's residence in Xima Pool. Director Huang of the Second Branch Bureau also searched out stolen gold jewelry, such as bracelets, from Master Tang's robbery case in a manure pit. People sent by Master Tang's household identified the items as the original stolen goods. The Criminal Investigation Team is currently conducting a detailed investigation. County Magistrate Wu highly commended the Criminal Investigation Team for solving two robbery cases in one day and awarded them 100 yuan, and the Public Security Bureau awarded them 40 yuan, which were distributed to the officers as a reward.

Wuxi

Shenchang Silk Factory Burns Down

The Shenchang Silk Factory, located outside the Guangfu Gate at the East City Foot, was previously established by local residents Yang Zhongzi and Yuan Duanfu. Due to the sharp decline in the silk market, it was unprofitable and closed down last month. Subsequently, Chen Zisun from Suzhou invested money and cooperated with Yang and others to resume operations on the 1st of this month. Unexpectedly, around 11:00 PM on the night before (19th), a sudden fire broke out on the corridor connecting the machine pile and silk room in the factory. Manager Chen Zisun was horrified when he saw the situation and immediately shouted loudly, alarming all the employees in the factory and sounding the alarm. However, in an instant, the fire had spread to the silk room, breaking through the roof. The fire was so fierce that it was impossible to approach. After the fire brigades from various sections arrived and tried their best to extinguish the fire, they managed to save the accounting room and the raw cocoon room. The rest was reduced to ashes, with losses estimated at around 5-6,000 yuan. However, the factory had previously held fire insurance worth 20,000 taels with the Royal Insurance Company of Shanghai but had just canceled the insurance last month. It is said that the cause of the fire was due to the mischief of a deity. Afterwards, the responsible Public Security Second Branch Bureau summoned Manager Chen Zisun of the factory to the bureau for interrogation.

Bizarre Death Case at Xintang Bridge

A nameless male corpse was found in the river at Xintang Bridge, in the 558th Tu near Dongting in the Second District. The corpse was floating by the river, head down, body face down, with a rope around its neck and a blue stone tied to it. The situation was quite bizarre. The Tu Zheng, Bao Rongqing, came to the city to report to the local branch court for an autopsy. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Shen, leading the examiner Liu, went to the countryside to conduct the autopsy. The autopsy revealed minor injuries on both arms of the deceased, a slight opening in the left eye, an empty stomach, urine discharge, swollen scrotum, and no feces in the anus. It was determined that the deceased had been tied to a blue stone while alive, thrown into the river, and died. After the autopsy, he ordered the Tu Zheng to collect the body and brought the blue stone and all the belongings of the deceased to the court for safekeeping in order to investigate and handle the case.

Changzhou

Notorious Robber Yu Congchang Executed by Firing Squad

Last year, a notorious robber broke into the home of Zhao Qingping, a gentry in Qingguo Lane in Wuyi City, and shot and killed the gatekeeper, He Canhai, with a gun, robbing him of property and other items. After the incident occurred, it caused a sensation for a while. It was generally believed that the robber was very skilled. The county government and the public security organs ordered his arrest. This year, the Public Security First Branch Bureau arrested the principal offender, Yu Congchang, in another case and sent him to the county government for interrogation. The suspect repeatedly denied and recanted his confession. Only recently did he tacitly acknowledge his guilt. The county government proposed a death sentence and submitted it to the provincial government, which telegraphed its approval for execution by firing squad on the 19th. This morning (20th) at 10:00 AM, the county magistrate dispatched police to take the suspect Yu Congchang into custody, verify his identity, and bind him to Fengweidun for execution by firing squad.

Apart from the Boy Scout street collections, which have already ended, other general donations are still in progress. Yesterday, schools came to the association to submit donations, including 53 yuan in silver dollars and 1249 jiao in small coins from the First China Elementary School, 11.5 yuan in silver dollars and 164 jiao in small coins, 867 copper coins from Hualong Elementary School, 24 yuan in silver dollars and 378 jiao in small coins from Qianye Junior High School, 396 jiao in small coins from the Provincial Shanghai Experimental Elementary School, 10 yuan in silver dollars and 246 jiao in small coins from Chaozong Elementary School, 83 yuan in silver dollars and 489 jiao in small coins, 35 copper coins from Qingxin Girls' High School, 1 yuan in silver dollars and 80 jiao in small coins from Minzu Elementary School, 2 yuan in silver dollars and 64 jiao in small coins from Shagang Elementary School, 74.5 yuan in silver dollars from Kaiming Middle School, 30 yuan in silver dollars and 187 jiao in small coins from Huaixing Elementary School, 18 yuan in silver dollars and 562 jiao in small coins from the Municipal Chongzheng Elementary School, 3 yuan in silver dollars and 41 jiao in small coins from Xintang Elementary School, 68 yuan and 8 fen in silver dollars from the Poor Children's Education Institute Elementary and Middle School, and 10 yuan in silver dollars and 192 jiao in small coins from Songxue Elementary School. The schools that received general donation receipts from the association included the First Elementary School of the French Concession, Zhuhang Elementary School, Minzu Elementary School, etc.

The previous street collection by the Boy Scouts was quite successful, but due to the short time of only one day, it was difficult to be universal. It is hoped that all residents in the city will embrace the heart of "saving disaster victims is saving people, saving people is saving oneself," enthusiastically donate, and together achieve good deeds. The deductions from factory workers' donations sent to Shanghai Bank have been very enthusiastic in recent days. Yesterday, 5 yuan in silver dollars was opened by Huachang Weaving Factory, 10 yuan in silver dollars was opened by all employees of Huachang Weaving Factory, 17 yuan in silver dollars was opened by Hexing Copper Bed Factory, 12.7 yuan in silver dollars was opened by Dongxin Sand Casting Machine Factory, and 65.96 yuan in silver dollars was opened by Huachang Match Hard Sheet Company. It is also reported that many trade associations have been sending donations to the Emergency Relief Association in recent days. Yesterday, the Woolen Goods Trade Association sent 50 yuan in silver dollars, and other trade associations are in the process of soliciting donations. It is expected that the results will be considerable in the future.

The Emergency Relief General Donation Association has been discussing with leaders from all walks of life regarding donations from the wealthy and has determined the grade standards for the amount of donations from the wealthy. It is reported that solicitation will begin on the 22nd.

Municipal and County Jointly Owned Assets

Evaluation Meeting Held Yesterday

The joint accumulation of grains, funds, and existing properties of Shanghai City and County have been repeatedly analyzed at meetings by representatives of both parties, but without results for a long time. The Municipal Finance Bureau has submitted an order to the Municipal Government for approval to survey, estimate, and divide the accumulation of grains, funds, and existing properties together. Representatives of both the city and county held an evaluation committee for jointly owned assets of the city and county at the Municipal Finance Bureau yesterday. As a result, seven representatives were appointed to re-evaluate. The county representatives submitted the principles determined by the county government affairs meeting as a reference for the evaluation meeting, with the following principles: (1) The county still insists on surveying and estimating the two types of assets together, and after estimating the price, dividing the property and management according to the proportions that the city and county should receive. (2) After valuing the industrial land, it should be evenly distributed in advance with fertile and barren land matching each other. For those odd lots whose prices cannot match the city's six and the county's three, the two parties can make up the difference with cash. If the city still insists on auctioning off the property and dividing the funds, the county should request the right to inherit the assessed bid price and give priority to specifying the property as the winning bid. (3) Since the Shanghai Hospital is retained by the city, it should be uniformly valued and included in the city's share. (4) Existing assets and accumulated grain funds should be handled in the same way. After division, if the property obtained by the county has already been occupied by the city, it should be immediately transferred for acceptance. If it is needed in fact and cannot be transferred for a while, the rent should be paid according to the market value.

The Municipal Party Headquarters Will Organize Aid for Impoverished Party Members

The Party Voice is Scheduled to be Published on February 1st Next Year

The Publication Fee Will Be Deposited in a Bank to Generate Interest for Relief

According to 국민社, the Municipal Party Headquarters of this city, for the purpose of instilling knowledge among all Party members in the city and providing relief to impoverished Party members, has decided to fund the publication of a semi-monthly magazine called "Shanghai Party Voice." The content will be substantial and is sure to satisfy readers. The annual subscription price is set at two silver dollars. The proceeds from the subscription fees will be organized into a management committee, deposited in a bank to generate interest, and a method for using the interest to provide relief to impoverished Party members will be established. The organizational regulations for the management committee and the relief measures have been approved by the Municipal Executive Committee. Details are listed below:

Management Regulations: "Organizational Regulations for the Shanghai Party Voice Subscription Fee Management Committee." Article 1: These regulations are established in accordance with the provisions of item 6 of the Shanghai Party Voice Printing Regulations. Article 2: This committee will be organized by one executive committee member, one supervisory committee member, and one Party member representative elected by the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee to manage the subscription fees for the Shanghai Party Voice. Article 3: The aforementioned subscription fees shall be deposited in a secure bank, and only the interest may be withdrawn; the principal shall not be touched.

Article 4: When the committee withdraws the interest from the subscription fees, it shall follow the orders of the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee and must be signed and sealed by all management committee members. Article 5: The term of office for the committee members shall be the same as the term of office for the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive and Supervisory Committee members of that term. Article 6: The committee shall have one chairman, who shall be the representative of the Executive Committee members. Article 7: All committee members shall serve without pay. Article 8: The committee shall be located within the Shanghai Special Municipality Party Headquarters. Article 9: These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee.

Relief Measures: "Provisional Measures for Providing Relief to Impoverished Party Members with Shanghai Party Voice Subscription Fees." Article 1: These measures are established in accordance with the provisions of item 6 of the Shanghai Party Voice Printing Regulations. Article 2: The Shanghai Party Voice subscription fees shall be deposited in a bank designated by the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Municipal Executive Committee) to serve as a fund for providing relief to impoverished Party members. Article 3: The deposited subscription fees shall be managed by a management committee organized by one executive committee member, one supervisory committee member, and one Party member representative nominated by the Municipal Executive Committee. Article 4: In the event of the death of an impoverished Party member, their family may request, with proof from the standing committee member of their original district branch, that the Municipal Executive Committee provide appropriate funeral expenses, but the amount shall not exceed thirty dollars. Article 5: If an impoverished Party member has been unemployed for more than two months, they may, by providing a statement of facts, request, with proof from the standing committee member of their original district branch, that the Municipal Executive Committee provide living expenses, but the amount shall not exceed ten dollars per instance, and no more than three times per year. Article 6: The Party members applying for relief in the previous two articles must have resided in this city for more than one year. Article 7: Those applying for living subsidies should provide appropriate labor during the period they are receiving assistance, as designated by the Municipal Executive Committee at any time. Article 8: These measures may be amended at any time if there are any matters that are not fully covered. Article 9: These measures shall be implemented on a date to be determined and announced separately after approval by the Municipal Executive Committee.

The Peiping-Hankow and Nanking-Wuhu Railways

Water-Land Intermodal Transport to Be Implemented on New Year's Day

Contracts Signed Sequentially

Great Convenience for Passengers

The Peiping-Hankow Railway's water-land intermodal transport faced difficulties in the construction of the Pu'an barges at the Jiang'an in Hankow. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company specially dispatched a commissioner to Hankow to excavate the Jiangbian Road, using giant iron chains to pass through the road and build cement and steel pilings to secure the barge. This matter has been settled. Now, the company has agreed with the Peiping-Hankow Railway to implement the intermodal transport on January 1st. Details are as follows:

Implementation on New Year's Day: The Peiping-Hankow Railway's water-land intermodal transport contract was signed in March of this year. At that time, due to the issue of freight rates, the prices of foreign merchant ships on the Yangtze River route fell sharply, especially for intermodal cargo such as Xuchang tobacco. The railway and shipping companies repeatedly discussed this matter and revised the contract. Furthermore, the construction of the barge at Jiang'an in Hankow faced difficulties, leading to repeated postponements of the implementation date. It was not until the 20th of this month that the Pu'an barge was finally completed, allowing for the loading and unloading of goods. The company and the railway bureau then discussed and decided to implement the intermodal transport starting on New Year's Day.

Civil Aviation: Private shipping companies in Shanghai can also participate in this intermodal transport. On the Yangtze River route, there are the Sanbei, Ningbo-Shaoxing, and other private shipping companies. Various private aviation companies have requested the organization of a joint office, to be composed of personnel appointed by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and Sanbei, etc. This was previously submitted to the Ministry of Communications, and approval has now been received that it is not necessary to establish a separate office. When the intermodal transport volume on the Peiping-Hankow Railway is not yet crowded, the China Merchants, Sanbei, and Ningbo-Shaoxing shipping companies will use their existing Yangtze River ships to handle the intermodal cargo. However, the warehouse in Shanghai will be designated separately, and the accounts, etc., will be established separately by the company's intermodal transport division to be distributed to the private aviation companies. In the future, when the intermodal transport volume becomes crowded, special ships will be dispatched to transport directly to various ports in Nanhua. The Nanking-Wuhu Intermodal Transport: The Jiangnan Railway Company has currently constructed a railway from Wuhu to Sunjiabu in Xuancheng, totaling over 180 kilometers. Xuancheng is the wealthiest grain-producing area in Anhui Province, producing rice, wheat, rapeseed, and Xuancheng paper. More than two million dan are transported to Shanghai and Zhejiang each year. Historically, transportation has been done by sailboats due to inconvenient transportation. Now that the Xuancheng-Wuhu section of the Jiangnan Railway has been completed, grain from Sunjiabu can be transported by train. Mr. Zhou, the transportation director of the railway, has agreed with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company on an intermodal transport contract. The details of the intermodal transport for the Wuhu-Xuancheng section have been signed.

Simultaneous Trial Operation: To operate the intermodal transport first on the Wuhu-Xuancheng section, the construction of the Nanking-Wuhu section will take another four months to complete. The company has dispatched Mr. Jin Jin, an officer from the intermodal transport division, to Wuhu to investigate the cargo transport on the Wuhu-Xuancheng section and negotiate the intermodal transport procedures. According to Mr. Jin's investigation, the main inbound cargo is grain, and the main outbound cargo is tobacco, kerosene, wheat flour, salt, sugar, hardware, seafood, and yarn. They have traditionally been transported by private boats. Now that Mr. Jin, representing the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, has reached an agreement with the Jiangnan Railway, it is planned to start the trial operation of the Wuhu-Xuancheng intermodal transport on New Year's Day, simultaneously with the Peiping-Hankow Railway. After the completion of the Nanking-Wuhu section, it will be added to the intermodal transport. The Wuhu-Xuancheng intermodal transport will not conflict with the business of the Yangtze River ships. It will replace the transportation by private sailboats with train-boat intermodal transport. The water freight will be cheaper, and the time will be faster. Passengers can also handle remittances, and the convenience is not limited to these few points.

Li Jingcong Talks About the New Initiatives of the Eurasia Company

Relocating the Airport and Replacing with New Aircraft

Re-electing a Portion of the Directors and Supervisors

The Eurasia Aviation Corporation recently held a board meeting and a shareholders' meeting, approving the company's financial statements for the 22nd year and many other important matters. A Central News Agency reporter specially visited Mr. Li Jingcong, the general manager of the company, yesterday morning. According to him, the relocation of the airport has been completed, and passengers have been boarding and disembarking at the new site since Sunday of last week. The meeting the day before yesterday was to present a report on the process. The following is a record of Mr. Li's remarks:

Airport Relocation: According to Mr. Li, the company's airport relocation has been underway for a long time. The site is located on the west bank of the Huangpu River, adjacent to the north of the China National Aviation Corporation's airport. It covers an area of 800 square meters, and the acquisition of private land has been completed. Temporary office buildings and hangars have been built. Since Sunday of last week (the 16th), passengers have begun to board and disembark at that location. Yesterday's board meeting was to present a report on the relocation process and to submit the budget for the construction of the hangars for discussion and resolution. Replacing with Large Aircraft: The company currently has three W34 aircraft and three W33 aircraft. The former has a larger fuselage and more passenger seats, while the latter is smaller. This was also discussed at the meeting the other day. Because the company's routes are very long and there are more passengers, it was decided to exchange the original three smaller W33 aircraft with the German Lufthansa Airlines for two W34 aircraft. Once the new aircraft are shipped to China, the old aircraft will be shipped back.

Approval of Financial Statements: At the shareholders' meeting, in addition to the company submitting the financial statements for the 22nd year, which were discussed and approved by the meeting, the Chinese director Shen Yani submitted a resignation request, which was approved. Du Dianying was re-elected to succeed him. Furthermore, the term of office for the company's supervisor Cheng Yuanfan has expired, and Wang Yansong has been appointed to replace him.

Zhang Xiaolin and Four Others Elected as Chinese Directors

Wu Kaisheng Appointed as a Chinese Commissioner to Negotiate

The Construction of Qiaole Village is Nearing Completion

The Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission Announces Registration for Displaced Overseas Chinese

The First Phase Will Accommodate 200 People, Limited to Men

After Receiving Certificates, They Can Reside in the Village and Engage in Reclamation and Animal Husbandry

In order to find ways to assist returning overseas Chinese, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission has leased wasteland in Xuancheng County, Anhui Province, to build Qiaole Village, to accommodate overseas Chinese for land reclamation, to provide assistance. Yesterday, it specially announced the registration for returning unemployed displaced overseas Chinese, the original text of which reads (omitted above): In order to assist unemployed returning overseas Chinese, this commission has leased wasteland in Cixi Town, Xuancheng County, Anhui Province, to build Qiaole Village, to accommodate unemployed returning overseas Chinese for residence and cultivation. The first phase is limited to 200 men. Any unemployed returning overseas Chinese who are interested in rural business and meet the following conditions may come to register, including (A) carrying an overseas Chinese registration certificate and sufficient documents to prove that they are indeed unemployed overseas Chinese; (B) having a responsible letter of introduction from overseas Chinese associations or local Party headquarters embassies; (C) being between the ages of seventeen and sixty, having the ability to cultivate and herd livestock, being hardworking and enduring, not addicted to bad habits, and having no chronic diseases. (Explanation) Those who meet items A and C can be said to have the above-mentioned documents. Together with the application form, come to the Commission (or write to the Commission at Moling Road, Nanjing) to register starting on the 15th of this month and wait for review and accommodation in order. Once approved, a permit and land license will be issued, allowing them to reside in the village and engage in reclamation and animal husbandry. However, the reclamation methods are divided into three types: (1) self-funded reclamation; (2) reclamation with loans; (3) cooperative reclamation. They must be declared separately when applying. The Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission's Committee for Assisting Unemployed Overseas Chinese.

The Garrison Headquarters

Executed Red Pill Offender Duan Yongsheng Yesterday by Firing Squad

Addicted to Strong Narcotics, Relapsed After Rehabilitation

And Set Up a Red Pill Den for People to Use

Duan Yongsheng, a native of Shandong, lived on Qiujiang Road in Zhabei. In June or July of this year, he was arrested by the police for using red pills and sent to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters. After being ordered by the doctor to quit the drug addiction, he was released on bail. However, after being released, he not only relapsed

but also opened a lit place for people to use red pills. On October 3, he was again arrested by Police Chief Hao Likai and other police officers from the Zhongxing Road Police Station of the Xinzha Branch, along with users Wang Laowu, Zhu Kangjiu, and Hou Zhengming, and red pill paraphernalia were seized. They were all sent to the bureau and presented to the Garrison Headquarters for interrogation. After clear interrogation by the military court of the Garrison Headquarters, the defendant Duan Yongsheng was found to be addicted to strong narcotics, relapsed after rehabilitation, and profited from setting up a place for people to use them. According to Article 4, last paragraph, and Article 5, last paragraph, of the Provisional Regulations on Strict Prohibition of Strong Narcotics, he was sentenced to death. The defendant Wang Laowu, also known as Li Mingcai, was previously arrested on June 23 of this year for using red pills and sent to the doctor for rehabilitation. He has now relapsed, undoubtedly a repeat offender. However, considering his ignorance and relapse due to illness, his situation is still pitiable. He was given a reduced sentence of twelve years of imprisonment. The defendants Hou Zhengming and Zhu Kangjiu were both first-time offenders and were all sent to the doctor for rehabilitation. Hou Zhengming was released on bail, but Zhu Kangjiu was a squad leader transported by the Shanghai Seachang Public Bureau's resident new recruits reception station. As a soldier, he indulged in bad habits. After rehabilitation, he should be sent to the Shanghai Homeless People's Work Training Center to serve for three years. It is now learned that this case has been reported by the Garrison Headquarters to the Nanchang Camp for approval. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Duan Yongsheng was taken into custody and escorted by military police to an open space next to the Longhua Airport for execution by firing squad. The Garrison Headquarters' announcement is recorded as follows: The case of Duan Yongsheng, presented by the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau for intending to profit from setting up a place for people to use strong narcotics and for relapsing after rehabilitation from strong narcotics, has been received by the headquarters. The military court was ordered to handle it according to law and judge that Duan Yongsheng intended to profit from setting up a place for people to use strong narcotics and was sentenced to death, and he was sentenced to death for relapsing after rehabilitation from using strong narcotics. The death sentences were combined and executed. The volume and judgment were also inspected and submitted to the Nanchang Camp of the Chairman of the Military Commission for approval on file. In addition to verifying the name and identity of Duan Yongsheng, binding him and taking him to the execution ground for execution by firing squad to show [severity], this announcement is jointly issued to inform the public. This announcement, December 20th, 23rd year of the Republic of China, Concurrently Commander Wu Tiecheng.

Exchange Federation Pushes for Representative Petition

Gu Xin Yi and Mu Ouchu Go to Beijing

Departed Last Night

The Exchange Federation, in order to request the Central Government to temporarily postpone the collection of transaction tax, again appointed Gu Xin Yi and Mu Ouchu as representatives of the Exchange Federation, and carrying a petition, they took the night express train to Beijing at 11:00 PM last night to meet with the Central Authorities and request a temporary postponement of implementation. The original text is as follows:

The Three Major Functions of the Exchange In the modern economic organization, the exchange has three major functions: forming prices, transferring risks, and circulating materials. The exchange is the center of the continuing market, gathering a large amount of supply and demand, seeking mutual convergence, and determining appropriate prices as the official market price.

1. Forming Buying and Selling Prices This official market price can directly serve as a standard for the buying and selling prices of those involved in material transactions, and indirectly as a guide to the changing trends in the economic sphere. However, the rise and fall of the official market price of the exchange can indicate the actual supply and demand of the goods and the accurate credit of the securities. Producers, guided by this market price, can prepare in advance. If there is a trend of supply exceeding demand, they reduce their production. If there is a trend of demand exceeding supply, they increase their production, so that the supply of materials does not suffer from the disadvantage of excess or deficiency, and then they can safely implement "market production". The exchange, guided by this market price, can know the underlying meaning of supply and demand and make fair transactions. Investors, guided by this market price, can know what to do, choose the short and avoid the long, and make profitable investments. Not only that, but the exchange also has futures trading, so that if there are differences in supply and demand between locations A and B, and between near and far times, the market price will be different. Then, purchase where supply is abundant and sell where demand is high, playing the role of shortening the long and supplementing the short, and achieving the effect of drawing from one to add to the other. The supply and demand of different times and places can be adjusted, and the prices of different times and places can also be leveled. This is why the exchange is a price-forming mechanism in modern economic organization, and why Article 19 of our Exchange Law stipulates that "the exchange shall determine, announce, and publicize market prices."

2. Risk Transfer Mechanism In the modern economic organization, in addition to laborers and capitalists, there is also the existence of the business sector. Entrepreneurs are those who operate businesses with their own plans, and at the same time, they also bear the risks of business operation. Therefore, if an enterprise wants to develop, it must find ways to minimize the risks it faces. The modern exchange operates with a large amount of supply and demand, regular trading methods, and the reference of speculative traders. Therefore, the future crises caused by production by entrepreneurs can be transferred to speculators through hedging (hedging trading). Generally, there is a time difference between the purchase of raw materials and the production of products in all production industries, and there will be changes in supply and demand and fluctuations in market prices during this time difference. However, knowing that the prices of raw materials and the prices of products tend to rise and fall in unison, it is possible to pre-sell raw materials and products of the same month in the exchange at the same time as purchasing raw materials. In this way, if the market price rises later, the losses in the exchange can be compensated by the raw material purchase. If the market price falls in the future, the losses in the raw material purchase can be compensated by the exchange. As a result of hedging, the risks faced by entrepreneurs in production can be borne by speculators in the exchange, and producers can safely engage in production. This is why the exchange is a risk transfer mechanism in modern economic organization.

3. Material Circulation Mechanism Today's market production is mostly the accumulation of shares, so the buying and selling of a product and the raising of a company's shares must have a central agency to gather its supply and demand. Otherwise, buyers and sellers are scattered in all directions, and funds do not flow regularly. Convergence is not easy, and transactions are even more difficult. Those with huge capital do not know where to purchase and do not know where to invest. Even if there is the mediation of intermediaries, the negotiation of prices, the identification of quality and credit, and the performance of contract terms are not necessarily reliable. With the establishment of the exchange, a large amount of supply and demand is concentrated, the system of guaranteeing buying and selling is established, and transactions can be completed at any time and in any quantity. Prices are fair, grades are clear, credit is evident, and procedures are extremely simple, facilitating transactions, smoothing the transfer of materials and the circulation of capital. This is why the exchange is a material circulation mechanism in modern economic organization. The exchange has such economic functions in modern society, and it is even more impossible to ignore it under the current situation in our country. Today, a large number of products in our country, such as cotton, yarn, and grain, are squeezed by foreigners, and the shortening of sales channels is not uncommon. If each industry has an exchange organization, the masters of the industry will manage the affairs of the industry, the news will be well-informed, opportunities will not be missed, the planning will be meticulous, and the market conditions can be maintained. With real power in the hands of each industry, it will not be manipulated by foreigners. This is another function of the exchange under the current situation in China. Therefore, for the sake of economic development, for the sake of rescuing the depression, and for the sake of competing with foreigners, it is necessary to support its growing trend at present.

The Disadvantages of Taxing the Exchange The establishment of formal exchanges in our country originated after the seventh year of the Republic of China. After the turmoil of the tenth year of the Republic of China, the foundation gradually became stable. Over the past ten years, they have been painstakingly managed, and have created today's situation, and have fulfilled their due responsibilities. Now, our government levies transaction tax on exchanges. In terms of academic theory, this is a matter of course. How dare merchants hold different views on this? However, in fact, under the current situation in our country, the problem of implementing the collection of transaction tax is not whether the tax law is intended or not, but the concern is how the associated disadvantages will be. Once the exchange is taxed, brokers, for their own benefit, will inevitably take the following two paths. First, brokers, for the sake of current interests, pass on the burden to clients and increase the handling fees for buying and selling. Second, brokers, for the sake of future interests, endure the burden for a while, maintain the original handling fee rate, in order to attract buying and selling orders. Of these two, one must be chosen. Now, first, from the result of brokers increasing the handling fees for buying and selling, we can deduce the consequences that should be dealt with.

After the Handling Fee for Buying and Selling is Increased After the handling fee for buying and selling is increased, the direct result will inevitably affect the decline in buying and selling. In today's commercial depression and market decline, this decline in buying and selling is an inevitable fact. The exchange will also inevitably be led to a state of stagnation. The function of the exchange has been described above. Its role in the modern economic organization is like the heart of the human body. The blood vessels of the whole body enter the heart, and then circulate throughout the body, developing into strength. Now, if the heart reduces its effectiveness, the whole body will suffer. The disadvantages of exchange stagnation are the same as this, and the depressed commercial situation will become more depressed, and the stagnant materials will become more stagnant. This is one thing that cannot be ignored. Today, the largest transaction in our securities market is government bonds. In recent years, due to financial deficits, the treasury's allocation relies heavily on bond issuance. If transaction tax is also levied on the buying and selling of government bonds, the result in the future will inevitably lead to the stagnation of old bonds and the difficulty of issuing new bonds. This is the second thing that cannot be ignored. Moreover, during the national crisis, everything is waiting to be done. In recent years, various provinces have been working hard on construction, and the materials for construction rely on the issuance of debt bonds to serve as funds. The best way to raise this kind of public debt is to hold it in the securities market. In terms of the future trend of local bonds in various provinces, there will inevitably be an opening day in the near future. Now, if the exchange's buying and selling expenses increase, buying and selling will not be easy, indirectly blocking the road to provincial bond issuance. This is the third thing that cannot be ignored. Our country's securities market has always had few stocks on the market. In the past year or two, although one or two dozen types have started trading in Shanghai, the number is still limited. Although China's enterprises have not been developed due to various internal reasons, China's economy is ultimately booming, and the development of enterprises is expected. Now, if there is one more obstacle to buying and selling on the exchange, there will be one more difficulty in the transfer of stocks. Therefore, it is difficult for established enterprises to develop, and it is difficult for unfinished enterprises to be produced. This is the fourth thing that cannot be ignored. Our country's national industrial industry flourished during the height of the European War. The most notable among them are cotton yarn and flour. The products of both of these are indispensable to our people's livelihood. However, after the world economic panic occurred, the surplus products of various countries flooded in, and the neighboring country of Japan was particularly strong. Products such as yarn and cloth flour were all competing with our national products at the lowest price. Those with weak capital have collapsed one after another, and those with slightly thicker capital have also entered the last breath. Now, if the commodity exchange that circulates materials is increased by one more obstacle, then the factories in this last breath may also be reduced without ending the morning, and give a great blow to the national industrial industry. This is the fifth thing that cannot be ignored.

Maintaining the Broker's Handling Fee The result of brokers increasing the handling fee for buying and selling is as described above. Now, from the perspective of brokers maintaining the current handling fee, we can deduce the points that can be worried about. In fact, today, the handling fees charged by brokers to clients in various exchanges are often lower than the fixed amount due to the depressed market conditions. Now, if there is another layer of transaction tax burden, the most worrying thing is that it may lead to illegal "external transfer" transactions within the exchange. External transfer transactions are buying and selling that is conducted privately at the exchange market price without going through the exchange market. There are two types of external transfer: one is external transfer from Broker A to Broker B, and the other is external transfer from Client A and Client B at the same broker. External transfer is an illegal act and is strictly prohibited by the Exchange Law (Article 38). However, where the profit lies, and because the losses increase, it is difficult to avoid breaking the law. As a result of external transfer, not only does buying and selling lose the protection of the exchange, but also since buying and selling does not go through the exchange, the exchange has no way to know the broker's trading volume. Therefore, on the one hand, transactions can be leaked, and on the other hand, if there are too many external transfers, the exchange's commission income will be reduced, and profits will be reduced. Therefore, the business tax originally paid by the exchange based on profits will also be greatly reduced, and harm the national treasury's income. At this point, if the government gains from this (transaction tax) and loses from that (business tax), is it not still useless to finance? This is the first thing that cannot be ignored. Taking a step back, even if brokers endure losses, they may be able to barely sustain them temporarily at present. However, after a long time, the accumulated losses will inevitably affect the survival of the exchange. Unfortunately, if the Japanese "exchange" which is not subject to our laws rises up, deliberately disrupting the situation, then our country's exchanges will inevitably have to shut down all operations. If it comes to this point, then the prices of our country's products will inevitably have to listen to foreigners again. The exchange that has been fought for for more than ten years will be handed over to others again. Is there anything in the world that is more heartbreaking than this? This is another thing that cannot be ignored. In summary, although the collection of transaction tax is theoretically indisputable, there may be many difficulties in implementation. It is necessary to carefully study the tax rate so that the aforementioned disadvantages can be reduced to the minimum. Otherwise, the effectiveness of the tax collection has not been seen, and the economic crisis will occur immediately. This is not the original intention of our government's tax collection. Therefore, rather than failing in the end, it is better to be cautious at the beginning. Merchants are not intelligent and only state what they see as an aid to the government's administration, and dare not deliberately create alarming words to sensationalize.

The Gospel of the Disaster Victims in Julidan Three Counties

The Society received a letter from Commissioner Li from Liyang yesterday, reporting the distribution of relief in great detail. The extracts are as follows (the above is omitted). After the review was completed, 37,000 bags of relief flour were purchased and transported. A joint meeting was held with the heads of the China Foreign Famine Relief Commission, the Shanghai Zhiyuan Buddhist Society, the Wuxi Swastika Society, the Pu Ren Charity Association, and other relief workers. The reviewed household registrations were re-examined, balanced and distributed, and it was decided that each Swastika ticket would be distributed with 50 jin, Pu ticket 30 jin, and Hui ticket 20 jin, in order to show fairness. It was also stipulated that the first district would be released from the 8th to the 11th for three days, the second district on the 12th, and the third district would continue to be released on the 16th, releasing for three days in each district. On the day of the relief distribution, Tianzhen invited representatives from all walks of life in the party and government to monitor the distribution. In the second district, 2,308 households received Swastika tickets, 3,163 households received Pu tickets, and 1,822 households received Hui tickets. In the fifth district, 2,981 households received Swastika tickets, 5,010 households received Pu tickets, and 2,315 households received Hui tickets. In the sixth district, 87 households received Swastika tickets, 936 households received Pu tickets, and 2,554 households received Hui tickets. In addition, 120 households were added to the Swastika. In total, 11,541 households received Swastika tickets, 15,605 households received Pu tickets, 13,837 households received Hui tickets, and 720 households received Swastika tickets, for a total of 37,650 bags of flour. This relief effort achieved such good results, entirely due to the joint efforts of the various charitable organizations. Those who promoted and supported this matter were mainly Li Dixian, He Zhongxiao, Lu Bohong, Cai Quchen, and Tang Huikang. Cai Quchen, in particular, was busy in Shanghai and Xixing, arranging fundraising, which is especially commendable. Once the relief work in Li is completed, it can be started soon, etc.
