Free Discussion

Qualifications of a Critic

— Xinren

We have read many articles about criticism, but they all seem to lack a basis. For example, criticism should be correct, critics should be fair, and so on. However, it seems that not many people emphasize the importance of the critic's own life experience. In fact, this point is a crucial element for criticism.

Writers should have profound life experiences, and critics are no exception. If a critic is detached from life's realities, he cannot understand the life reflected in the work. He may quote extensively and write impressive critical essays, but such criticism (if it can be called criticism at all) is irrelevant to the writer and the reader. Because he can only rely on his own narrow subjectivity, he is prone to making superficial and erroneous judgments.

Of course, a critic must have a broad understanding of artistic theories, but as the cornerstone of his worldview, he should also be familiar with social sciences and even natural sciences, and grasp the correct methodology. Art criticism analyzes the degree of truthfulness of the reality reflected in the work, elucidates the author's consciousness and attitude towards society and life, and thereby attaches social value to the work. Artists use images to construct works, while critics use logic to analyze them. The tools critics use to express their ideas are the same as those of science, and critics always touch upon social issues when analyzing works. Therefore, social sciences and even natural sciences are essential basic knowledge for critics. On this foundation, they can then build their specialized knowledge of criticism.

However, just as technical skill alone cannot make a true writer, theoretical cultivation alone cannot make a critic. They must also have profound life experience, because only through life experience can they understand reality. Criticism is ridiculed by writers partly because in today's society, "fairness" is not absolute but relative; it is fair to the majority but not to the privileged few. Therefore, current criticism either receives welcome from the majority and ridicule from the minority, or vice versa. On the other hand, the lack of life experience and correct understanding on the part of critics is also a key factor in criticism being ridiculed. In this case, critical theory becomes dogma, becomes constitution, and the critic becomes an empty commander.

A true critic possesses both correct theoretical knowledge and profound life experience. He can understand the writer's creative process and all aspects of life. He can concretely help writers complete great works. The greatest mistake in the world is the one we make without realizing it, and critics have the responsibility to point out the writer's negligence, difficulties, and errors. In this way, creation is enriched by criticism, and criticism will also be enriched by creation.

Only those with such "qualifications" can be considered "critics."

Waste of Water

— Lingmo

Returning to my hometown, I realized that this year's famine is far more severe than I knew. In our small village, the surrounding fields are known to be free from drought and flood, but also because they are considered good fields, the ideal standard is to harvest four or five *shi* of grain per *mu*. We have never seen this standard reached; every year we hear that the harvest is not good. Although this year's disaster is quite widespread, our area has never felt the threat of drought. It is located by the river, and we can utilize the tide. This year the tide is not small, so in theory, we should not feel a lack of water. So, the talk of a bad harvest is just the same old story, right?

My guess was not entirely wrong. In a larger area, the so-called tidal towns and *wei* nearby, which constantly feel the threat of water and rely on earthen dikes for life, have all opened the dikes to draw water this year, and irrigation is very good, with almost a full harvest—their standards are originally lower. But in our small place, the main fields are not by the river, but on both sides of a small river. Two or three *li* from the river mouth, the riverbank is almost level with high tide; two or three *li* further up, high tide reaches half the river; above that, the tide cannot reach, but the river is in the valley of a small mountain, and usually after the snow melts or after several spring rains, the mountain water can accumulate to fill the river. Originally, there were earthen dams in sections to store water, but they are rarely used. In recent years, there has been too much water, and often because water was originally stored, sudden mountain water comes and cannot be discharged in time, which damages the fields. The function of the dams has gradually been forgotten, and the dams have gradually been washed away by the mountain water, leaving only remnants. The mud flows into the river and into the Yangtze River. Some sediment settles midway, some flows to the river mouth and is pushed back by the tide, resting at the river mouth. Very little actually flows into the Yangtze River. As a result, the riverbed rises day by day, and the river mouth silts up day by day. When the tide comes, no plans are made. After the tide goes out, we wait another half month. Half a month later, everyone draws water, but the manpower and tools for drawing water are not enough to manage, and the crops cannot wait another half month. So we sit and wait for famine.

Because of this year's lesson, the locals also thought of repairing the river, in addition to preparing to dig it deeper, they are still building dams. This decision has not yet been implemented and is feared to be delayed until next year. If next year is a water year again, this proposal will eventually disappear. In a place that averages over 1,000 millimeters of rainfall per year, the neglect of water storage is very obvious. In fact, there is no way to not neglect it. If we prepare to store water but do not know what the fundamental solution is, just following the methods of storing water in dry land really feels like a redundant tumor when the rainfall is balanced.

A small river in my hometown is a very small issue, of course, but by analogy, the situation of larger rivers, even the Yangtze River and the Nile River, is similar. Usually, we only fear that the water in the river does not flow fast enough, and when it floods, we only complain that the lakes and marshes downstream are not large enough to store water. We never think that the source above will be cut off, so we never bother to prevent the source from being completely exhausted. Before the British built the Nile Dam, the Egyptians never considered the flooding of the great river to be irresistible, and never felt that too much water was wasted, when this excess water could have been diverted for other uses.

Of course, projects like the Nile River cannot necessarily be applied to the Yangtze River, and even the smallest project may not be worth implementing on a small river like the one in my hometown. However, there must be many similar methods that can be adopted. I do not have the knowledge to specifically point out which one, but suppose there were reservoirs in Dabie Mountain, Hongze Lake could reduce flooding, and the upstream could reap more irrigation benefits. Also, if Shaanxi had plateau lakes like Dianchi Lake in Yunnan, it would not suffer from repeated droughts. Although there are no natural ones, it seems not impossible to remedy them with artificial ones.

It seems that the result is the same old saying: it depends on human effort. Most river channels have already fallen into disrepair because of human inaction. As long as we start doing it again, no matter which aspect we start with, it will only be better. But I think the upstream water should be a more fundamental and convenient solution.

Returning from the Volcano (1)

— Lanru

The goddess of autumn arrives gracefully in the world, just when I am leaving my warm southern country. Now that I see her quietly departing, I feel endless sorrow and melancholy in my heart. I curse winter, that death-freezing demon. Once it arrives in the world, the howling north wind, the torrential rain, the gloom, the darkness, everything follows.

Autumn in Japan is beautiful. The number of young men and women, poets and literati viewing the autumn leaves may even be greater than those viewing the cherry blossoms. Although I did not see the autumn leaves this time, my friends laughed at me for failing to live up to autumn. However, I feel that I have not only not failed to live up to it, but I have completely possessed it. Although it was only a short day's work, I feel that the beauty of autumn in the human world has been admired by me alone.

Ever since I heard Mr. Qin propose a trip to Mount Mihara volcano, I was so excited that I hardly slept all night. I thought, even if I didn't have a penny, I would borrow money from friends to travel this time. It doesn't matter if I don't go to Nikko Hakone, but this famous volcano, the site of suicides, I must explore it once. I begged several friends to go with me, but they all answered me in tones of surprise and warning:

"It's dangerous! You can't go there!" Several newly acquainted Japanese friends, when they heard that I was going to Mount Mihara, all stuck out their tongues and said, "It's dangerous! Don't say goodbye to us!"

But I finally went.

Who is Going to Sayonara? (Note)

At 8:30 on the evening of November 10th, our party of seven arrived at Reigan Island. Mr. Qin went to buy tickets for us, and we all stood in the waiting room observing the expressions on each traveler's face.

"Look, let's guess who in here is going to sayonara." Mr. Jingyi reminded us to pay more attention to and scrutinize each traveler's expression and tone of voice.

The ship docked outside the door of the waiting room. As soon as the door opened, everyone boarded the ship in the order they were standing. This seemed to be a new discovery for me. I forgot that this was an island. Like a villager coming to the city for the first time, I felt surprised. Why can the ship go ashore?

Because we arrived relatively late, the good cabins were all taken by those who went ahead. We squeezed into the steerage at the stern of the ship, with only a foot of space for each person to lie down.

The ship departed at 9:00. I heard it would take until 4:30 the next morning to reach Oshima Island. This long night was a bit frightening. The sea breeze was strong, and we didn't bring blankets. We could have rented one on the ship for twenty cents, but because there were so many tourists today, even blankets were not available for rent. Actually, we could have taken off our clothes to use as blankets, but the only thing I had never experienced in my life was the crowding of people against people. On both sides were Japanese people. Only Ms. Yang and I were Chinese. They squeezed tightly against us, sometimes even putting their feet on us. I tried my best to kick them away, but after a while, they would come again.

Sky Bridge

— Zigang

The tram tracks stop in the middle of the plaza, with cloth curtains and stalls on both sides, leaving only a few pedestrian walkways for people to pass through.

Coming on foot or stepping down from trams and rickshaws, the footprints of those who ride in cars probably wouldn't appear here. Here, you really feel the prosperity of China's population. The sound of people helps your eyes, making you feel like it's a dazzling scene, with people like bees among flowers, sucking up the nectar and still panting.

The hawkers' cries:

"Bargain sale! Six plates for half a dollar, two piles for a dollar!"

"Foreign flower bunting, one dollar for two *zhang*!"

It sounds so energetic, sung as a tune, repeated over and over again, with the blue veins on their temples bulging. Why not find Japanese trademarks on those clever little toys? But now the wave of inspecting Japanese goods has passed, and buyers and sellers understand each other tacitly. On the other hand, the copper and tinware shining in the sunlight are genuine Chinese goods. The old woman is there picking incense burners and candle holders, and the tea-addicted old men are suspiciously eyeing the purple copper teapots, feeling for the coins in their pockets.

In the used clothing store, under the apprentices' singing and laughter, old cotton-padded jackets and broken cotton quilts are being flipped through. Winter has arrived, and men who can't redeem anything from the pawnshop come to browse these stalls, carefully negotiating the price:

"Too expensive, the lining is completely yellowed and blackened. Who knows what the cotton inside is like..."

"We can take it apart and show you, the price is fair." The young clerk is excited to see someone asking, most afraid of those who look and shake their heads and leave.

The fortune-teller's table has a human face hanging on it, with the ears, eyes, nose, and lips filled with words like a map. Few people are absentmindedly throwing money anymore; people are slowly using their money for more practical purposes. Sixteen coins can buy a brown dried cake!

Women with rolled-up trouser legs linger in front of the paper flower stalls, and newlywed brides with painted faces and red and green robes are also strolling on the bridge, asking this and that in low voices, and hurriedly dodging when the water carriers come to sprinkle soil on the road, wearing rose-red embroidered shoes.

The street performers' stalls are crowded with people watching the "eighteen transformations." If you're unlucky, you're forced to throw in a big coin; if you're smart, you watch half of it and slip away. Those eloquent and energetic heroes of the streets perform one routine after another, with saliva flying straight into the faces of the audience.

Bicycles skillfully weave through the crowd, and the bicycle shop is piled with old bikes and parts.

A sign is posted in front of the teahouse: "Water money, one large coin; upstairs, three small coins." But it's really full of friends in short clothes. Those who go upstairs to look out are wearing an air of arrogance and pride.

The busiest places here are the leather goods stores. Clerks walk up three steps and pull at customers, their energetic cries reminiscent of the prostitutes on Sima Road. These leather shops are clustered in groups of five or six, struggling to survive even though customers are so rare.

Going south from the Sky Bridge is the execution ground. Curious people inquire about the news, and old hands will stroke their chins and smile:

"They executed one this morning, without even interrogating him first!"

People flow like water toward the Sky Bridge. There is no high threshold here. Many people below the poverty line remember it. Although this Sky Bridge seems to be a Ground Bridge, filled with people sighing in life, in their eyes, it is a Sky Bridge in hell.

Cocoon (1)

— (Original by Hayao Hayashi) Translated by Jingzi

Whenever I see cocoons, I think of Sakai Yasuo. However, I am now a city person—a city person who can only see decorations of the moon and reeds in shop windows to feel that autumn has arrived. I no longer have the opportunity to see the single-wheeled carts carrying raw cocoon cages swaying along the country roads where flying crows knock down the fruits of the rough-leaved trees.

× × × ×

Sakai and I were friends in middle school. In the same dormitory, in the same room, we sat side by side at small desks, loving each other like twins.

Behind the middle school was a hill covered with small pine trees. In early summer, many wildflowers were scattered around the roots of these small pines, and small snakes with striped patterns meandered in these white wildflower clumps.

"A sharp and bright thing!"

Sometimes, he would always say this in a sentimental way while chasing after the small snake, whose scales reflected the early summer sun, quietly hiding in the flower clumps.

"A sharp and bright thing!" Saying this sentence probably had some meaning for him. Because he was often called a "dirty thing" by his ill-tempered classmates, a nickname that shattered his fragile little soul. He always wore tattered clothes. Therefore, when he talked about the snake, it probably contained some envy. He was born with a clever mind and always ranked first in his class. It could be said that he was extremely intelligent, but it could also be said that he was extremely poor, which was a very good contrast to me, who was neither very intelligent nor very poor. I was his only confidant and his only sympathizer. If he owed tuition, I would unhesitatingly take out part of my allowance.

In short, in the middle school dormitory at the foot of the hill, we sat side by side at small desks, loving each other like twins.

From the top of the hill, you could see the sea. The two middle school students often climbed this hill, throwing small stones that would never reach the blue paint dish under the clear sky. Sometimes, they would sing the out-of-tune "Amour River" duet while walking down this hill.

One day, we two were walking on the hill when we saw a snake swallowing a frog. The snake seemed to be opening its mouth so wide that its lower jaw was about to fall off. The suction cups of the frog's feet were exposed outside the snake's mouth, trembling as if begging for help. I saw Sakai's eyebrows twitching. Suddenly, his gray-white shoes kicked the snake's body desperately, and then he stepped on the snake's head with his shoes. A red thread of blood flowed from the flat yellow snake lips. He cursed angrily:

"Beast!"

The frog was finally saved. Its head was covered with the sticky saliva of the snake, and it lay motionless on the grass.

"Beast! Beast!"

Sakai cursed angrily again. About the snake, I only remember this one incident.

Finance: Floating Long Positions Continue to be Liquidated

Benchmark Gold Falls Two Yuan

丨Major Players Vigorously Buy to Provide Significant Support丨

Yesterday's gold market saw a strong rise in British silver, a general market weakness, and the continued liquidation of floating long positions. However, due to HSBC's vigorous buying of shillings and Dachen's efforts to buy in, the day's market conditions were maintained. It was easier to rise than to fall during the day. Montri forward silver prices rose three to four li, exchange rates slightly contracted, and London spot gold rose by half a penny. The benchmark gold standard price was listed at 1006.1 yuan, which had little impact. The morning opened with a low market, which was extremely stable after the opening, hovering only. However, because major players had a strong buying appetite and floating short positions also entered the market, the situation gradually improved. Banks also engaged in cover-buying. HSBC's listed exchange rates for British and American currencies remained unchanged, and demand exceeded supply after entry, once rebounding. However, due to pressure from those taking advantage of high prices, the price gradually fell. It still struggled, but morale was not greatly boosted. Sellers continued to be active, and the domestic market gradually loosened. Sellers took the opportunity to be active, so even though the exchange market was stable, it still declined. After that, the overall market was stable, hovering only. It was observed that the market sentiment was tired throughout the day, and the remaining floating long positions continued to be liquidated, but the strength was ultimately weak, so Dachen was able to become the mainstay. Oil Market

Production Area Suffers Shortfall, Shanghai Inventory is Meager

New Season Rapeseed Oil Actively Soaring

Since the arrival of new rapeseed oil on the market, the market situation has become serious. Inventories everywhere have been exhausted. Zhejiang Province produces the earliest new oil, but this year, western Zhejiang is the most deficient. Compared to last year, it only accounts for 30%. Therefore, not only is there no oil available for sale in the Shanghai market, but Shanghai merchants are also purchasing Jing oil to make up for the shortfall. In the Shanghai market, whenever the new season arrives, new oil from Zhejiang Province is bound to arrive in abundance. Therefore, Shanghai merchants usually do not prepare much stock at that time. However, this year, the situation is the opposite. No new oil has arrived from Zhejiang Province, and merchants from Jiangxi Province are purchasing goods in Hankou instead. The new production areas in Zhejiang and Jiangxi provinces used to have a surplus, but now they are stretched. Since all areas cannot obtain new oil, they are flocking to the Hankou market to purchase old oil for sale. However, the old oil reserves in Hankou are not abundant. Once various merchants rush to purchase, the remaining stock is unexpectedly swept away. Subsequently, the goods en route are gradually sold out, and prices soar. The cost of transporting Jing and Han oil has increased to 12 taels. New goods from Macheng are arriving in succession, with four to five hundred pieces. All are being borrowed by various merchants. The asking price is likely to be between 11.5 and 11.6 taels. Recently, various regions have been sending letters to stop borrowing oil for fear that the borrowing will lead to a large price swing in the future, and they will wait for the opening before purchasing. Only about 50 pieces of Jiangxi oil arrived in this port. It is estimated that the price will be above 19 yuan. The oil is slightly damp. During this time of shortage, the distribution among various firms is barely sufficient, not to mention selection. The total market inventory is less than 500 pieces. With only this meager stock for a large city like Shanghai during peak sales, it is truly alarming. Therefore, the current selling price of heavy Jing oil has increased to 20 yuan per piece, but there is still no spot oil available and one must wait for the oil to be loaded. Jiaxing local oil needs to reach Shanghai at around 23 yuan, about 3 yuan higher than Jing oil. Users do not find it cost-effective, so no one has purchased it so far.

Sugar Market: Local Factory Refined White Sugar Continues to Rise by 0.2 Yuan

Yesterday, the sugar market continued to be tight. The association's benchmark price for 24 raw granulated sugar was 18.6 yuan for ordinary spot goods on the previous day. Those that had not been sold were sold yesterday for 18.62 yuan. The price of local factory goods rose by another 0.05 yuan to 18.7 yuan. Transshipment goods remained unchanged at 5.2 yuan. #8-9 Dutch red sugar was 14 yuan, and the next grade was 13.8 yuan, with transshipment goods at 4.9 yuan. Taikoo Sugar B brand rose by 0.05 yuan to 19.45 yuan. The price of local factory refined white sugar was also tight. Zhenyu No. 1 was 17.9 yuan, and No. 2 was 17.7 yuan, both rising by 0.2 yuan. No. 3 was 17.5 yuan, rising by 0.15 yuan, and No. 4 was 17.3 yuan, rising by 0.1 yuan. The Guangzhou wheel of the Taikoo Company arrived in Xinchao Qing yesterday from Swatow with 4,000 bags. Samples have not yet been seen, but the market is expected to open today, and there is likely to be a loosening trend.

Page 17

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Love Letter Auction

— Niu

Napoleon was originally a maverick of the world. He was both a despotic tyrant and an affectionate man. Therefore, he had many romantic affairs during his lifetime. According to a London telegram on the 17th, "Auction houses here today auctioned Napoleon's love letters. These love letters were sent by Napoleon to Queen Marie Louise, totaling 318 letters." Another telegram stated, "The French government recently purchased 300 handwritten letters from Napoleon I for £15,000, many of which have not been published." Another telegram stated, "Last year, eight love letters from Napoleon to his lover Josephine were sold for a total of £4,400."

Calculated in this way, the value of a love letter from Napoleon ranges from £50 to £550. The huge price of his love letters can be imagined. Therefore, the London auction house sold 318 love letters from Napoleon the day before yesterday for only £15,000, which is really very cheap. It is probably also due to the sluggishness of the British market, so it is still a blood-drenched bargain sale.

Speaking of love letters, my country produces the most in quantity, as rich as if they were manufactured by machines. Students above middle school, no matter how professors jump and shout on the podium, lecturing with gusto and in a flowery manner, like a feverish fool, but some students often squat in the corners of the classroom to write their love letters, hearing nothing. The clerks in the shops, because of the sluggish market and dull business, are also secretly writing love letters on the counters like dragons and snakes, very happily. If you have the power to check each post office every day, I guarantee you will find thousands, or at least hundreds, of love letters every day.

If these love letters were sold like Napoleon's love letters, not to mention the price of each love letter being £450, even if they were sold at a blood-drenched sacrifice, at a cheap price, with each love letter selling for only £50, I think not only can my country's national debt be completely repaid, but also my country's construction undertakings, and the airplanes and cannons used during the war, can all be funded with the price of love letters, and there would be more than enough. Wouldn't that be wonderful?

I once heard people say that love saves the country, and I was puzzled. How can love save the country? Only now do I know that, besides "flirting with the eyes and promising with the heart," love letters are an important tool. So-called love saving the country is actually love letters saving the country. I advise a few affectionate seeds to quickly write love letters to save the country.

Speechless

— Ming

(Anecdotal Experience)

The day before yesterday, I took the train back to Songjiang for some business. I left early and returned late, buying a round-trip ticket to save a dime and five cents, which was a small but welcome saving. On the way back, I was extremely bored. Fortunately, I met a friend, Mr. So-and-so, and we chatted freely. We talked about world affairs, and then about a Songjiang middle school graduate who became a robber. (Because that day, the Rifeng Silver Shop on Songjiang West Gate Street was robbed, and the robber's name was Zhao Zhiyi, a graduate of Xuhui Public School.) We all gasped deeply, really having nothing to say.

Soon, the train arrived at Xin Zhuang. As usual, the tea room attendant came to collect the tea money. All friends who drink tea must "stretch their waists" and "break the bank." A passenger sitting next to me asked the attendant, how much is the tea money? The attendant replied, twenty cents. The man immediately looked surprised, saying, twenty cents for a cup of plain tea? How do you think the attendant replied? Sir, look at those gentlemen, some of whom normally don't drink tea. The gentlemen who do drink tea must be used to having everything. They definitely won't haggle over this. The man had nothing to say, so he took out twenty cents and gave it to the attendant.

My friend then said, when you go out, you should always act generously; you must not haggle over small things. This man haggled over a small thing, and even we were subjected to his "covert criticism." This attendant is really hateful, but there are many like him. If you haven't seen the world, you're bound to "hit your head" and "get a face full of dust" when you go out. Therefore, you must have some experience when you go out and know the "rules." Confucius said, "When entering a territory, ask what is prohibited; when entering a country, ask about customs," which is the same principle. The other day, I heard a few things that made me blush and become speechless. Let me tell you about them..." (The following are facts told by my friend.)

My friend, Mr. So-and-so, returned from Shanghai to Songjiang the other day, taking a second-class train. Midway, he felt a bit hungry, so he ordered

Page 18

a plate of curry chicken rice. After eating, he asked how much it cost. The waiter replied, thirty cents. Mr. So-and-so said, I'm used to paying twenty-five cents; I've never paid thirty cents. The waiter smiled and replied, sir, you're used to sitting in third class; this is second class, so it must be thirty cents. Mr. So-and-so had nothing to say.

My friend also said, last month, I went to a restaurant with two or three friends. We ordered a few dishes casually, including a "zha ba." Later, when the bill came, the "zha ba" was priced at eighty cents. I was surprised it was so expensive. I said, "zha ba" is just a small dish; you want to sell it to us for eighty cents? The waiter then smiled and said, sir, do you know what "zha ba" is? I was stunned. How could I know its origins? The waiter, seeing that I couldn't answer, then said, what is "zha ba"? "Zha ba" is taking a whole young chicken, removing the head, feet, and shoulders, cutting it into eight pieces, and then frying it in a pan. That's called "zha ba kuai." Selling you a chicken for eighty cents, how can you say it's expensive? I also had nothing to say.

There's one more thing. This summer, I came to Shanghai with three friends to shop. After eating dinner, we were very bored in the hotel. Mr. So-and-so suggested, why don't we hire a car to take a ride? It's really boring to sit here. Three yuan for an hour can exchange for some fresh air and see the scenery of the foreign concession. I was the first to agree, and the other two friends also said it was a good idea. So, we called a convertible car from a nearby car company, specifying an hour's ride. At that time, Mr. So-and-so looked at his watch, which was 9:45. So, we went from the main road to the Bund, to Jing'an Temple, and other places. After a while, the driver said the time was up. The car stopped. Mr. So-and-so took out his watch and looked. It wasn't even 10:30 yet. So, he said to the driver, we started at 9:45, and it's not even 10:30 now. How can you say the time is up? The driver looked at the watch on his wrist, snorted, and said, I bought my watch for one hundred and twenty taels of silver. How can your few-dollar watch be accurate? Mr. So-and-so also had nothing to say.

Winter Droppings

— Shixing

Beside the Stove

Seeing the chimney extending from the crystal-clear glass window of the house opposite, slowly emitting warm smoke, my wife said sadly...

"When will we be able to install a stove!"

"It's early."

"But isn't there already a thick layer of frost on the roof tiles at night?"

"But shouldn't we endure the cold as we endure poverty, and strengthen ourselves in the cold?"

"I know you're deliberately trying to freeze me to death."

I couldn't help but get angry at such hysterical, unfeeling words... "Then why did you marry a poor wretch like me?" I mocked her like that. To avoid arguing with her, I walked out, but regretted it when I got to the street. It was November, the beginning of winter. I could endure the cold, but what reason was there to force my wife, who was wearing a thin cotton robe and suffering from a lingering illness, to endure the cold with me?

The people in the movie theater seemed to have forgotten winter.

The next day, I pawned my only ornament, my engagement ring, and rented a stove. In the evening, I lit a fire in the house.

Looking at the friendly firelight emerging from the burning coals in the corner of the room, I happily raised my head... "Come sit by the stove," I said to my wife, but I saw a quiet, tearful, haggard face.

"Why, why are you still crying like that? Isn't there already a stove, and haven't you been consumed enough by sorrow?"

My wife stared at me for a long time, then said with pity... "A stove is too luxurious for us!"

It was incomprehensible that my very vain wife would consider a stove a luxury, and wasn't she the one who asked for it? As I was wondering, she stroked my face and said... "Look at yourself; this year of poverty has already turned you into a thirty-year-old middle-aged man."

Shaking off her hand, I sat down silently by the stove. My heart was like being covered in dust, becoming increasingly gloomy, while outside the window, the early winter, cold and dim twilight was spreading.

Life

— Jia Chen

I do not believe that there is anything in life that is worthy of praise or nostalgia. Except for the time of childhood when one is ignorant of everything, living the life of Adam and Eve in the primitive age. Once out of the paradise of childhood, and called an adult, one is also forever separated from the beautiful realm of the Garden of Eden, and even more forever separated from the enjoyment of happiness. On the one hand, one steps into the path of suffering, and from then on, one wanders and suffers on the path of suffering. Suffering all kinds of disasters and setbacks, bearing the burden of life, the millstone of life, year after year, day after day, letting that burden, letting that millstone press down, and everyone is pressed under the millstone, panting and struggling, until the ability to struggle disappears completely, so that one is no longer walking, but crawling, and then gradually bends the neck, hunches the back, and after a long time, perhaps from a strong person, becomes a pile of skin and bones like firewood, and from being completely like a person to being completely unlike a person, at this time, one is about to be finished.

But no matter who it is, they must stubbornly live on, even if they are stark naked, leaving only a bare body, they still cherish their worthless life infinitely, and live on, perhaps there is still a little hope. With this idea, even if they are starving every day and cannot make a living, they are still attached to life, unwilling to return. They would rather let the millstone of life pressing on their heads crush them so that they cannot move, and still refuse to let go, desperately supporting the millstone, struggling, falling down, then climbing up again, climbing up, and falling down again, and so on until they finally have no strength left. People are so full of the desire to live, what is it for? It is really incomprehensible. Often I see a kind of disabled person, whose limbs, which are the tools for earning a living, are incomplete, but they still turn their incomplete bodies and shout on the road, begging passers-by for a penny. Does such a person's life still have any interest and hope? I do not understand why they still insist on living in this way. I imagine that they would be much happier dead than alive, but they insist on living, and demand the same as ordinary people, which is too incomprehensible.

If it is said that the Creator has given you a life, you must naturally live, but how will you live? Is it just living by eating three meals a day and sleeping? Is it just living by a person being born, growing up, marrying, having children, growing old, and dying? If this is considered living, if this is considered life, then so-called life is fundamentally a bit ridiculous. However, most of those called people live in this way. And living like this, not living is not a big deal, and living is not a big deal either. Living a lifetime is the same as not living.

But the reason why everyone insists on living is probably because everyone holds half a hope for their own life, and there is a kind of beautiful longing growing in their hearts, calling them to sell their strength, and therefore they have a strong interest. So, it doesn't matter if the millstone of life crushes them until they are pale and emaciated, without a word of complaint, and without discouragement. However, what is considered a longing for life, or an ideal, does not really exist, and even if it does, it is as vague as a cloud in the sky. At best, it is nothing more than deceiving oneself, just to comfort oneself, and because of this, many people are willing to support the millstone, full of the idea that the days of being gilded will come later. Just keep thinking. Turning ordinary life into extraordinary. As if life will really be as grand as one thinks. In the end, the so-called longing is just a dream, and dreams will never bear fruit, or even turn into a pile of ashes, and nothing else is obtained. Only a few disappointments and emptiness are obtained. How can an ordinary life become extraordinary? In the end, it is still living a lifetime of incomprehensible life. It is still confused.

However, for the sake of that so-called longing for life that is not easy to come true, people all put on different faces, clownish, fierce, complicated like the painted faces on the stage. At the same time, they all use their minds, watching each other, taking advantage of a moment of carelessness, they kick you down, and step on top of you, watching each other in this way. Whoever has any loopholes, they will attack. And often in order to take advantage, they may as well put their conscience aside and let others suffer. At the same time, even if they are proud, those who step on others will eventually be stepped on by others. And in the end, the millstone of life on their own heads will also crush them so that they cannot breathe.

Is that what life is all about?

Gray Zone

— Sakura No

A child's wandering.

He did not know whether he lost his father after birth or his father died a day or a year before he was born; he did not see clearly what his mother's face looked like was kind and amiable, but when he just opened his eyes, it was when his mother closed her eyes 丨So, a lonely child was left to begin wandering.

He was half-lucky to receive the pity of a mother who had just lost her first son, and was accepted as this mother's son, and his body was kept warm and fed by this mother's milk.

The mother cared for him as if he were her own son, and took great care to look after the health of the surrogate child.

Slowly, the child grew up in the process 丨 Able to not drink milk, able to speak, and able to go alone from one village head to another village head and back again, without asking for directions and without making mistakes!

In the evening, he was able to easily feel that he was a lonely child without parents, but he would also sob privately out of gratitude for the cultivation and enthusiasm of this mother!

He was filial to this mother in direct proportion to the mother's care for this child, the love and concern of natural human relations!

One night, the mother fell ill, very seriously ill. Her face turned as pale as the waxed paper wrapping on cigarettes 丨

He rushed to invite Fang the doctor back, and the second time he saw his second mother's eyes closed tightly again, and he cried out loud!

His uncles and aunts rushed into the house and took all the belongings into custody.

He lost his nursing mother, and he lost his home.

After that, he began his second wandering.

He spent the night on the stone steps across the street with a large burlap sack.

The head was covered but the feet were not, and when he got up the next day, two feet had died!

His feet were so frozen and numb that he couldn't stand up, and he stumbled forward in a fall!

Wow! An extremely loud sound came from under his body, a girl of the same age, her face turning blue-purple, being crushed so that she couldn't breathe!

He took off his cotton coat and gave it to her to wear, cradled her head and neck and lay down in his arms, wrapping the burlap sack around his shoulders.

He rubbed the child's chest with his palms, and gradually a wisp of breath came out of her mouth.

He had found a confidante!

She was a lonely child without parents who had been driven out by her stepmother's lover.

They spent such a wandering life together!

One evening, it was so dark that they couldn't see anything, and they hadn't found a morning meal of pancakes.

Their stomachs were grumbling so loudly that they couldn't hold back, and they had no choice but to tighten their belts a little more. The flesh was so tight that it hurt!

The rice buckets of the bao fan makers were carried in front of them. Not caring about anything, they reached out and picked rice from the newspaper. Those makers rolled their eyes at them for a while, 丨Little beggars!

She complained that they shouldn't do such things, why should they be scolded as little beggars!

But her stomach was really hungry.

He let her eat first, but she refused to eat.

He cried and walked away.

When he came back, he saw that she was also crying terribly, and his heart ached even more!

The next day, he accompanied her back to her stepmother's house. He kowtowed desperately on the stone slabs several times, begging them to take in this poor child!

Under the sharp gaze of the neighbors on the left and right, the stepmother pulled her into the kitchen.

She saw him leaving the gate, and the tears couldn't stop flowing from her eyes.

He was wandering alone again!

One time, when he passed this gate again, that girl was dead!

He couldn't guess how she died?

God bless this child to be safe forever.

There were no tears in his eyes!

Page 19

Passion Flower

— Cheng Quan

(Plant Encyclopedia ··

"Passiflora, also known as Passion Flower, the petals are in the shape of a cross, symbolizing the passion of the Holy Christ on the cross, hence the name."

丨丨Passion on the cross!)

I left.

The night before I left, she sent me a small bunch of Passiflora, silvery white.

丨丨For the sake of life, is there anything worth being sentimental about? The whole world has to bow its head in the face of life. In this era, are there still no young men on the cross of life?

Pondering, feeling sentimental. And listening to her Croemi's voice...

丨丨The petals of the Passiflora symbolize the glorious passion of suffering in life; giving it to you, it symbolizes the glory of suffering in life, is it not good?

丨丨Good, thank you. Life may have its glorious passion of suffering, and that passion is glorious. Then you remember me like that.

丨丨Passion is glorious, I will remember you like that.

丨丨Thank you.

So, I left.

Leaving is for the sake of life, and also for the sake of my own youth; children in storms always like to use their youth as a weapon against the family, against society, against all unreasonableness.

The entire childhood was eroded in an old society like an ancient tomb, where there are rotten ancient corpses, frightening bones, and hardened soil that has accumulated into fossils... When one day, a wisp of withered soul awakens from the stratum, it feels unbearable suffocation, squirming... finally found an opportunity, left the ancient city of rotten corpses, left the declining home, without any sentimental tone, like the leaves in autumn, drifting to the vast world, one mile, and another mile.

One mile, and another mile, just wandering slowly, laughing, struggling; climbing the knife-like peaks in the morning, and diving into the explosive-like raging waves at night 丨丨丨 But it is said that this is also representative of the tragedy of life.

丨丨Is it really the tragedy of life? Doubted.

The one who answered me was her... "Yes."

I was shocked... She, I had known for a year; but could she also be a flower cultivated in the region?

But... a miracle, there was no mistake, she was also spending every tomorrow by sending away every today herself. In this way, we became friends on the life path like sparks.

We were friends; but, I found that she had something more than me, it is said, it was the passion on the cross of life.

Damn, are wanderers allowed to have passion?

But, the most damn thing is... I learned to be sentimental from her!

Cursing every day in front of the black sun... cursing her, cursing myself.

Spending a day into the night, the heart is like being twisted generally 丨丨All afraid, watching the days fly away one by one like the shadows of crows in the twilight, losing youth, maybe losing the weapon, losing the strength of life.

Thank God, I don't allow myself to live here anymore. In my heart, I only remember her sentence... "Throw yourself into life, wandering child, you must have the kind of passion that Saint Christ had on the cross."

So I left without a sound.

Carrying with me the bunch of Passiflora called passion flowers.

When the ship stopped at the pier, it was dusk. Hastily taking my things and walking ashore, looking at the Passiflora in the basket, it was withered.

Silently, I plucked off two white cross-shaped petals. Flattening them and clipping them in the pages of a book, I held the withered bouquet and waved it at the small river...

丨丨Passion and the cross, go to hell; in the face of life, even you have to give way.

Walking ashore, it was already dusk.

Zhongxi (1040) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening Piece "Divorce"

There are truly evil marital bonds in the world. Speaking of divorce, the heart aches. They have differing opinions and cannot live together. It's better than constantly bickering on the pillow. Some have secretly made new vows, forming a separate pair of lovebirds. Some are rebuilding their love nests, attracting phoenixes to gather. Some abandon the old to love the new, willingly becoming unfaithful. Some remarry, finding it difficult to conceal it from their original wives. Therefore, everyone has to negotiate. First, explain in detail the separation of the pair. Feelings of sorrow. Endless hatred. It's like seven provinces' steel knives piercing the heart. They arrange to hire lawyers and pay fees together. The beautiful flower branch will never reunite. Some shake hands and kiss affectionately before leaving. Some have children pulling at their clothes, tears never drying. Some angrily turn their heads, willingly parting forever. Some hypocritically still want to make amorous advances. Let's see how they each seek a partner to share dreams. I'm afraid they will still encounter the same problems sooner or later. Strangers, do not linger with the love. Holding the pipa again, hatred hangs heavy. Just end this fleeting marriage with a single stroke.

Her eyebrows are curved like a new moon. Her eyes ripple with gentle affection, and her posture is light. Her fragrant cheeks often add a touch of whiteness. Mystical beauty keeps her youthful. Her spring flower-like fingers are as white as jade. Her fingernails are dyed with henna, quite fashionable. Her powder-covered neck is truly stylish. Her breasts are exposed, revealing new powder. Her cheongsam is narrow and tight around her body. Her fragrant sweat drenches her like wontons. Her short trousers and long stockings are worn even on hot days, not fearing mosquito bites. Who can match this kind of blessing? Excessive indulgence and extravagance are inappropriate. (We most hope) that she eats frugally, dreams and wakes up quickly.
